Wang Shucheng chaired the meeting. The meeting was conducted with due ceremony, and various cases were discussed until 10:00 PM. The details of the meeting are described below: (A) Report Items: (1) The request to the National Government to continue to protect and return private power plants. Result: It has been approved and transferred to the Executive Yuan to order the Ministry of Industry to investigate and handle it. (2) The request to the Six Courts to revise Articles 2, 10, and 14 of the Supervisory Regulations. Result: Article 14 has been amended, and Article 2 has been interpreted. (3) The request to the Henan Provincial Government to return the Pu-Lin Electric Light Company, which was confiscated. Result: It has been returned to private management. (4) The request to the Executive Yuan to return the Bishu-Yan Electric Factory, which was confiscated. Result: It was approved that it should be submitted to the competent authorities for handling. (5) The business tax on electrical appliances and materials. Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces are set at 20 per mille. The request to reduce it. Result: The Ministry of Finance issued an order stating that in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Hubei, and other provinces, the electricity tax will be changed to 2 per mille based on turnover, the electrical appliance tax will be changed to 5 per mille, the transportation tax will be changed to 2 per mille, and the water supply tax will be exempted. The Northeast and other provinces are under review. (6) The Construction Committee sought opinions on the rules for banning illicit electricity use. This association contributed eight articles, requesting amendment and cessation. Result: They were all adopted and amended separately. (7) The request to the Hubei Provincial Government for the New-Ti Pu-Xin Electric Company's business area, where an industrial company is competing for business. Request to ban it. Result: The Hubei Construction Department approved and ordered the industrial company to stop business. (8) As of this month, a total of 70 companies have successively joined this association. (9) Tongzhou in Hebei, Qinhuangdao Qin-Yu, Qixin in Yue County, Anhui, Tunxi in Xiuning County, Xuzhou in Jiangsu, and Wanxian in Sichuan, the electric light companies have all newly joined this association. (10) The Jiangsu branch has changed its name to the Jiangsu Provincial Private Electric Industry Association. (11) A letter from the Ashihe Electric Light Company in Jilin was received, contacting the industry associations in Jilin and Heilongjiang to form a branch, and all companies joined this association. (12) The Executive Yuan instructed the Ministry of Industry that lawsuits involving unregistered companies will not be accepted. (B) Discussion Items: (1) The Guangdong branch requested to submit to the government a general order to all provinces and cities to implement the rules for checking theft of electricity and recovering electricity fees promulgated by the Construction Committee. The decision was passed as proposed. (2) The Beijing Electric Company proposed that the government amend or supplement the rules for banning illicit electricity use and inspect users' electrical installations. The decision was submitted to the government for review. (3) The Beijing Electric Company proposed that the Beijing Public Works Bureau change the company's power supply regulations. Request for relief. The decision was handed over to the Standing Committee for detailed discussion. (4) The Baoding Electric Light Company proposed that a student at Hebei University was injured by electricity, and the transformer was installed by the university itself. The company cannot be held responsible. The decision was to send a telegram to the Hebei authorities to handle the case impartially. (5) The Pinghu Electric Light Company proposed that the penalty for stealing electricity is too lenient. Request to amend the rules strictly. The decision was submitted to the Construction Committee for review. (6) The Jiaxing Electric Light Company proposed that gold is expensive and silver is cheap, materials are soaring, and the price of coal is rising. Request to appropriately increase the electricity price to maintain costs. The decision was to have the Standing Committee collect the opinions of various companies before reviewing it again. (7) The Wuxing Electric Light Company proposed that the installation and electricity fees for street lights are entirely supplied by the company, and the losses are unbearable. Request for relief. The decision was to send a letter to the Zhejiang Construction Department, requesting the county government to comply with the Executive Yuan's order and provide at least half the price. (8) Schedule a technical committee meeting and welcome Fei Futao back from Germany. The decision was to appoint Shen Sifang and Ding Chunzhi to be responsible for preparations. (9) The Fuzhou Electric Company proposed to implement supervisory regulations to protect the private electric power industry. The decision was submitted to the government for review. (10) The Changzhou and Zhenjiang companies jointly proposed that they ordered coal from a coal mine, but the coal was not delivered, affecting business. Request for relief. The decision was to submit to the government for review. (11) A temporary proposal was made to exempt electric poles from business fees to comply with the cancellation of harsh donations. The decision was submitted to the government for review. (12) A temporary proposal was made that Hebei should form a branch as soon as possible. The decision was to appoint the Beijing and Baoding companies to be responsible for preparations. (Other cases are omitted).

Zhang Lisheng's Troops Suppress Bandits in Eastern Anhui 82

Bengbu Dispatch: After Jiang Guochang, a notorious bandit in eastern Anhui, was killed by Zhang Lisheng's Second Cavalry Division last month, the remaining bandits, recently joined by the fierce bandit Mao Laoliu's gang, continue to roam and cause disturbances in the border area of Mengcheng, Huaiyuan, and Dingyuan counties. Zhang Shutian, commander of the Fourth Cavalry Brigade, has been dispatching teams to search and suppress them for days, achieving significant victories. Mao Laoliu's gang was recently surrounded by Zhang's troops at Lujiagang. The bandits initially put up a stubborn resistance from a blockhouse, but after a fierce attack by government troops, Mao Laoliu was killed at the foot of the blockhouse, and the fake battalion commander Little White Dragon was also killed. In this battle, over fifty bandits were killed, more than forty were burned to death, and a minor bandit leader named Liu Quanfa was captured alive. More than ten guns were seized, and more than fifty kidnapped men and women were rescued and returned to their families. The captured bandit Liu Quanfa was executed on the spot. Currently, Brigade Commander Zhang is ordering his regiments to conduct searches in separate directions towards the bandits' lairs in the Laojiashan and Zhongjiashan areas, aiming to thoroughly eliminate them. (April 5th)

Local Correspondence

Wuxi 83

The Department Orders All Steamship Companies to Obtain Navigation Certificates: The Jiangsu Construction Department previously ordered all shipping associations in various localities to ensure that inland steamships obtain navigation certificates before March 31st, and issued regulations for this purpose. The shipping associations in various localities informed the steamship companies, which collectively stated that complying with the department's regulations would create many obstacles and be difficult to implement. There was a need to apply for an extension and modify the procedures, which was jointly submitted by the Wujin and Wuxi shipping associations. The difficulties were divided into two points. Recently, a response was received from the Construction Department, stating: (1) After reviewing the navigation certificate regulations issued by this department for inland steamships, which were piloted last December, Article 2 requires filling in details of Ministry permits and customs notifications, etc. If the steamship companies have existing customs permits, they should have obtained them from customs long ago. Why did they wait until the deadline for certificate application at the end of March to request the association to forward the request? It is unavoidable to suspect deliberate delay. In addition to requiring each steamship company to obtain the permits from customs, we will tentatively allow forwarding of letters, but this cannot be used as an excuse for delay, violating the regulations. (2) Tugs with permits should fill them in as per the permits, and those without permits should obtain them from customs. However, all other items still need to be filled in according to the form, without needing to order the bureau to issue permits. This avoids delaying the deadline. Those using foreign-owned ships should declare it accordingly. As for the request for an extension of the certificate application deadline, it cannot be approved. They should immediately urge the steamship companies to comply with the regulations and submit their applications. If they dare to deliberately delay, they will be punished according to the law. Upon receiving the response, the Wuxi shipping association has already notified all steamship companies. A Major Fire at Longhua Temple Causes Many Casualties: The Longhua Temple at Tanbo Bridge, Twenty-Six Ward, outside the South Gate, was recently initiated by Wang Qinxu, the owner of the Hechu Sanmao Grocery Store, to hold an eighteen-day Longhua Society (i.e., Longhua Association). Over one hundred old Buddhist women from the city attended the meeting. Unexpectedly, yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, a fire suddenly broke out on the second floor of the temple. At the time, there was a strong wind, which fueled the fire, and it quickly spread. Various fire brigades rushed to the scene to put out the fire, and it was extinguished after 4:00 PM. It is estimated that six halls and upper and lower floors of the main Buddha hall were burned down, with losses of about four to five thousand taels of silver. Two old women, Li Wang and a child, Wang Jishou, were burned to death, and five people, including Dai Wang, Shao Zhou, and Su Cao, were burned and sent to Puren Hospital for treatment. One old woman, Zhu, was seriously injured and her life is in danger. Afterwards, the responsible Public Security Third Branch sent police to take Ai Da, the woman in charge of the temple, to the bureau and then to the county Public Security Bureau for interrogation. Also, at about 8:00 PM that evening, five buildings of the Xiafang of the Taifu Silk Factory in Luojiahama, under the Ta Bridge outside the South Gate, were also burned down, affecting thirteen households. Two children, A Shengniang's son, Gengsheng, and Zhao Agai's daughter, Ximei, were burned to death. In addition, at Kaihua temple, north of the Xida Bridge in Nanfangquan, the home of Lu Shiliang was also suddenly burned down at 7:00 PM that afternoon due to carelessness, with four new and old houses completely destroyed, estimated losses of around ten thousand yuan. A Vagrant Gang Demands Money Through Extortion and is Arrested: Gu Hu, a woman from Fuzhou, Ganke Township, Fifteenth District of the county, is 45 years old and works as a lime boat puller. The other day, when her cargo ship returned home from Shanghai, a gang of vagrants, including Liu Ating, Gao Arong, and Yu Baolin, broke into her house with thirty to forty people and demanded 300 yuan in extortion. Gu Hu had no choice but to be extorted 62 yuan. Afterwards, she reported the incident to the county Public Security Bureau, which dispatched police to arrest Liu Ating and strictly ordered the arrest of Gao and others for legal action.

A Corpse Retains a Lifelike Appearance After Half a Year: A resident surnamed Han in Han Lane, near Shitangwan, Sixteenth District of the county, is quite wealthy. His wife, Ding, passed away last August, and her coffin was temporarily placed in Ding Lane. Unexpectedly, some local ruffians, believing that Han was wealthy and might have buried valuables with his wife, dug up Ding's coffin in the middle of the night the other day. A gold ring and a pair of gold bracelets were stolen. The next day, Han discovered the theft and reburied Ding's coffin. However, although Ding had been dead for more than half a year, her complexion remained lifelike, so people called her a "stiff corpse." It is rare to see a corpse in a temporarily placed coffin not decompose.

Dispute Over Sandbar Reclamation Leads to Dam Destruction: Zhu Benliang, the township head of the fourteenth township in the fourth district of Shazhou, and others stated that after the Lanli Company built a sea dike in 1922, the silted land was gradually occupied by wealthy people from the city and countryside. Only the sandbar claims obtained by mud workers in exchange for labor have not yet been realized. Last spring, representatives Zhu Tingyan and others filed a lawsuit with Zhu Tinghua and Chen Qichang over the illegal sandbar enclosure. Unexpectedly, on the 23rd of last month, Chen Qichang, along with Ye Zengpei, Wang Yingnan, Sha Wenbiao, Tang Qiwei, and others, and Huang Zhifang, the director of the Third Branch of the Public Security Bureau, sent patrol officer Zhao Zhongpeng and others to forcibly enclose the land and arrest Mu Dashu. When they searched Chen Jinlong's home, the mud workers were outraged and mobilized people to confront the followers of Chen Qichang and the patrol officers of the Third Branch of the Public Security Bureau. Township Head Zhu and others believed that since the sandbar dispute was already in litigation, both parties should wait for a legal judgment and should not mobilize people to destroy the dike, and Director Huang Zhifang of the Third Branch should not be exploited to interfere in the land reclamation, causing disputes. Yesterday, they submitted a petition to the county government and the Public Security Bureau, requesting that they be quickly ordered to stop the activity.

Director Mao Negotiates Loans for the Cheng-Xi Highway: Since Mao Feng was appointed acting director of the Jiangyin Construction Bureau by the department, he came to office on the 3rd. Regarding the northern section of the Cheng-Xi Highway project, because the Cheng-Cai section's bridge piers have not been completed and the Qing-Yang section has not yet held a traffic opening ceremony, and the Cai-Qing section has not yet started construction, the completion of the entire road has no definite date. On the 4th, Director Mao met with the county magistrate at the county government to discuss ways to proceed with the northern section of the Cheng-Xi Highway. He also spoke with Shen Lunxu, the director of the Finance Bureau, and Wu Shuying, the chairman of the county Chamber of Commerce. Director Mao announced that the Cheng-Xi Highway is short of 30,000 yuan in funds. In addition to borrowing 10,000 yuan from the Xi-Cheng Long-Distance Bus Company, he planned to ask the Finance Bureau to borrow 10,000 yuan and the county Chamber of Commerce to borrow 10,000 yuan from various money houses to speed up the project so that the entire road can be opened to traffic by June 1st.

Zhenjiang 88

Citizens Petition for Funds to Build Riverbank Protection in Guazhou: Zhang Mingxuan, Zhang Bohua, Liu Changchun, Ji Tiantong, and other gentry, merchants, and citizens of Guazhou, across the river from Zhenjiang, stated that the riverbank on the east side of the Guazhou River has been collapsing frequently due to erosion by the river tide over the years. The bank built over the years since the Republic has almost completely collapsed, especially the collapsed area of the first dike, where the outer beach is only a few feet away from the bank at its closest point. The outer beach between the Ji Family and the Majia Port is only twenty-odd feet away from the bank. In an instant, when the tide rises, the bank will collapse. Therefore, they requested the provincial government to allocate funds for building riverbank protection so that the people inside the dike would not be displaced. The planned project would be approximately 1,400 to 1,500 feet long and would require 14,000 to 15,000 yuan. If only the dangerous areas are worked on, it would be about 700 to 800 feet long and would require 7,000 to 8,000 yuan. The exact construction plan will be decided after the provincial government conducts a survey.

Import of Fish and Seafood Without Bill of Lading is Prohibited: The Zhenjiang Customs Superintendent and Tax Commissioner issued a notice stating that, according to the Ministry of Finance, starting from May 1, 1931, all salted and fresh fish transported from foreign ports will not be allowed to be imported unless they are transported on authorized ships and have bills of lading. However, fish carried by domestic seagoing vessels that have obtained licenses from the Ministry of Industry or local government agencies will still be allowed to be declared and transported as usual.

Bandits Rob Peddler on Baimiao Road: Tian Fu, a farmer living outside the East Gate of this city, makes a living by selling firewood every day. After Tian Fu finished selling firewood, he went to the post office to collect the remittance and return home. Unexpectedly, when he was walking in the Yunhuaqiao alley in this city, a person suddenly grabbed Tian from behind, ordered him to hand over the money, or he would take his life. Poor Tian was ignorant and afraid to make a noise because there was no one around. He had no choice but to hand over the 20 yuan along with the two thousand-odd cash he earned from selling firewood to the bandit, who then left.

He immediately untied him and learned that his name was Jiang San. He worked as a laborer in Hankou and had returned to Qingjiang after injuring his hands and feet. He visited friends in Yangzhou but failed to find them, and in desperation, he committed suicide. Wei, feeling sorry for his poverty, raised 16 yuan to send him away.

Xiamen University Holds 10th Anniversary Celebration 98

Simultaneously Holds All-School Student Military Review and Opens Sports Day

Xiamen University was founded solely by the overseas Chinese businessman Chen Jiageng. It has been ten years since it opened in 1921. The facilities are complete and the buildings are magnificent. It currently has five colleges: Arts, Science, Law, Education, and Commerce, as well as an affiliated high school. The professors are all well-known figures in the country. The construction cost reached more than 1.4 million yuan, and the annual recurring expenses reached more than 1.7 million yuan. It is the first private university to be registered. The content is said to be particularly rich.

Central Film and Cultural Propaganda Committee (Continued) 99

(7) Propaganda for Industry and Commerce to Revitalize Industry: The phrase "revitalize industry" is familiar to us. However, in the market, almost all commodities are imported goods. Even with just the textile industry, the annual losses already amount to tens of millions of yuan, not to mention others. Today, people advocate for domestic goods as a catchphrase, but with little effect. Why is this? It is because the advocates do not use the right methods, and the entrepreneurs lack guidance. For today's plan, it is difficult to expect results without large-scale propaganda. If films can be used to introduce Western industrial manufacturing methods in detail, so that we can learn from them and make improvements, and if the rich resources of the interior of each province can be shown on the screen to facilitate the development of industrialists, while also demonstrating the advantages and disadvantages of using foreign goods versus domestic goods, making people visually shocked and subtly influenced, then it will benefit the development of our country's industry and commerce in no small way.

(8) Propaganda for Agriculture: Our country claims to be based on agriculture, but recently, according to customs reports, over 200 million yuan of foreign rice is imported each year. This matter is of great concern and has a significant impact on the national economy. However, what is the root cause? Everyone wants to have a bumper harvest, but they end up suffering from famine. How can that be? However, our country's farmers have limited knowledge, and the agricultural tools they use are old-fashioned and clumsy. All work relies on the weather. When there are floods or droughts, they are helpless. The root cause lies in the lack of knowledge. To remedy this, it is necessary to equip farmers with agricultural knowledge. For example, in the winter of 1928, an agricultural tool exhibition was held in the suburbs of Paris. People from all over came to participate, asking about prices or how to use the tools, and buying what they needed. Only the Japanese carried cameras, one to photograph the shapes and structures of various agricultural tools, and the other to photograph their use. I asked them sincerely as a friend, "What is your intention in photographing this film?" He replied, "I am commissioned by the government to be stationed in Europe to film various news items and new products in agriculture and industry to inform the people of our country. This method is more convenient and can announce the truth without omission. If I were to make drawings of the works in this exhibition, then translate and explain them, it would take several months, and the result would still be empty talk on paper. Whether the people of our country can understand the use of these new products would still be questionable. Now, it only takes fourteen days to send them to Tokyo, so that when our people see this film, it is as if they have personally experienced this conference and know how to imitate it." From this, we can see that the power of making films is not insignificant. Now that our country's farmers' knowledge is so shallow, if we can imitate the Japanese method and make films of the latest agricultural tools and their use in various countries to promote them among the people, it will enable ordinary farmers to compete to imitate them, and the increase in production can be expected in a short time.

(Propaganda) Colonizing Borders, Immigrating and Comforting Overseas Chinese: Prosperous areas in the interior are troubled by dense populations. People think it is easy to make a living in familiar places. However, they do not know that colonizing the borders, with vast fertile land and gold everywhere, has gone unnoticed. Although it is said that this is due to transportation obstacles and difficulty in traveling, the real reason is not only this. The people in the interior do not know the real situation of the border areas, so they dare not go there rashly. Now, if we can film the prosperity of Mongolia, Tibet, and other places and the methods of development, and promote them widely, with special awards from the government, so that the unemployed will be happy to go there to earn a living, then the number of vagrants will naturally decrease, and production will increase day by day. Not only will our people be able to live and work in peace and happiness, but the people of the world will also indirectly receive its benefits, because production will increase. Therefore, propaganda for colonizing borders and immigrating is an essential plan. Furthermore, overseas Chinese have long suffered from the oppression of imperialism. I wonder how many people want to return to their motherland. If the government can compile concrete plans for urgently needed construction projects, set up plans, and establish measures to protect overseas Chinese investment in their home country, then if even one-tenth of the thirty million overseas Chinese return to invest, it will be extremely easy to start various construction projects and will benefit the country and the people in no small way. Otherwise, the motherland will remain the motherland, and the overseas Chinese will remain overseas Chinese, with no connection to each other, and neither will benefit. However, to arouse their idea of returning to invest, we must rely on film propaganda. Overseas Chinese are tens of thousands of miles away and do not know the real situation of their motherland. Therefore, they are hesitant to wait and see. Now, if we can film the richness of the whole country and the stability of the country and screen them in various places, arousing the interest of overseas Chinese in returning to invest, it would be an essential plan for today.

The above are just a few of the most outstanding examples. If we can implement them one by one, the effects will be as such. If we can promote them extensively, the benefits will be unlimited. I offer my humble opinion. I welcome my countrymen to teach me if I am correct. (The End)

This City

Cai Yuanpei's Speech on the Criteria for Choosing a Profession 100

The China Vocational Education Society held its 19th academic lecture the day before yesterday, with over 130 attendees. They invited Cai Yuanpei to give a lecture titled "The Criteria for Choosing a Profession." Mr. Yang Weiyu from the society gave an introductory speech. Mr. Cai's main points were that professions can be divided into mental and physical labor. Mental laborers govern others, while physical laborers are governed. Mental laborers are inventors and politicians, while physical laborers are practitioners. However, there are right and wrong, beneficial and harmful distinctions. Since ancient times, our country's mistaken concepts of professions have buried talent. It should be known that professions have no distinction of high or low, noble or base; all are equal. Those that benefit the people are righteous professions. For example, farmers who plant tobacco seedlings, workers who create poisonous gas to harm people, and merchants who sell opium and monopolize the market are engaged in unrighteous professions. The government should protect and encourage people's professions, enabling everyone to be properly allocated according to their strengths. Public undertakings will then be able to make efforts to improve. Male and female professions should be based on a division of labor, each serving society according to their natural inclinations. Housekeeping is also an important profession for women. In summary, the most important principle for choosing a profession is to consider social needs and take the happiness of the masses as a prerequisite; one should not harm the public for personal comfort. The lecture lasted an hour, and the audience listened attentively and were moved. At the end, Mr. Yang expressed his thanks, and the meeting was dismissed. It is said that the next lecture (on the 11th) has been scheduled, with Mr. Shen Junyi, director of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Works, speaking on "The New Shanghai Plan." Mr. Shen is an industrial expert with extensive research on municipal affairs, and it is expected that he will contribute valuable insights at that time. Those who wish to attend the lecture are requested to obtain a lecture ticket from the society.

Zonal Football Tournament Opens Tomorrow 106

First Match: North China Team vs. Central China Team

Tomorrow at 4 PM at the Baseball Field

Sichuan-England Football Team's Representation of Southwest China Rejected

Full Schedule Set, Closing on the 12th

The National Zonal Championship Football Tournament will open tomorrow at 4 PM after the North China team arrived in Shanghai the night before last. The North China and Central China teams will play the first match, and the tournament will close on the 12th. The Sichuan-England team's eligibility to represent Southwest China was rejected at yesterday's meeting. Details of yesterday's news are as follows:

Delegation Holds Meeting 107

Yesterday at noon, representatives from each team gathered at the Chinese Sports Advancement Association. Attendees included Shen Silang, president of the association; Zhou Jiaqi, secretary; Ma Yuehan, representative of North China; Song Ruhai, representative of Central China; Le Xiurong, representative of East China; and Liu Guangmei, representative of the Sichuan-England Football Team. The meeting was chaired by Shen Silang.

Sichuan-England Representative's Right Rejected 108

The most important issue decided first was whether the Sichuan-England Football Team could represent Southwest China. Liu Guangmei, representative of Sichuan-England, stated that transportation in Southwest China was difficult and sports were underdeveloped. Chairman Liu Wenhui had sent a telegram requesting that Sichuan-England be allowed to attend, asking the conference to make an exception for the sake of promoting sports. However, the representatives believed that while promoting sports was important, they could not make an exception for the sake of the zonal tournament's future. If Sichuan-England could represent Southwest China, it would become a Shanghai zonal football tournament, which would be contrary to the spirit and principles of the national zonal tournament. If such a precedent were set, any team unable to attend in the future could ask residents living in that area to represent them, which would be difficult to imagine. Furthermore, the East China team included people from South China, so whom would they represent? This would become a problem. For the sake of the future, the request was unanimously rejected. However, for the sake of promoting sports, the conference could ask the association to send an official letter to the Sichuan provincial government, urging them to vigorously promote sports. They expressed great respect for the spirit of Sichuan-England. After more than two hours, a satisfactory solution was reached, and it was resolved to report the details to the Sichuan provincial government.

Competition Method and Schedule 109

Next, the competition method was decided. It was agreed to adopt a single round-robin system, with each team playing each other once. The tournament will open on the 8th and end on the 12th. The game time will be 90 minutes. If there is no winner, the game will be extended by 30 minutes. The schedule is as follows:

(1) North China vs. Central China, 4 PM on the 8th (2) East China vs. Central China, 4 PM on the 10th (3) North China vs. East China, 3 PM on the 12th

Central China Team Members Continue to Arrive 110

The Central China Football Team was organized by the Hankou Municipal Government and business community. Due to various reasons, some members could not arrive earlier. Yesterday, Tang Xingtian (secretary), Yuan Qingwu, Xiao Bo, and Jinhua Jin all rushed to Shanghai. Hearing that the games would start yesterday, they took a Wuchang ship and arrived in Nanjing on the evening of the 5th. Yesterday morning, they arrived in Shanghai by train from Nanjing.

North China and Central China Practiced Yesterday 111

Yesterday morning, the entire Central China Football Team, led by Song Ruhai, practiced at the Chinese Baseball Field. They worked hard and their skills were quite good. They first attacked the north goal and then practiced attacking the south goal, returning only in the middle of the day. In the afternoon, the North China team practiced on the field. Goalkeeper Huang Zhenquan performed very well. Dozens of spectators watched and applauded from time to time. The right wing was stronger. They drove away only at dusk. North China will be a strong opponent for East China, and there will be another fierce battle.

Results of This Year's Annual Cross-Country Race 112

Shanghai Sports Association Wins Both Titles

First in Individual and First in Team

Champion: French Verdun

Third: Bai Hong Ma Fengrui

Time: 44 minutes 45 seconds

This year's annual cross-country race was held yesterday morning, with a course of eight miles on Jiangwan Road. As a result, the Shanghai Sports Association's A team won both titles, first in the team and first in the individual. The champion was Verdun from the team, with a time of 44 minutes and 45 seconds. Bai Hong Ma Fengrui fought hard and took third place, which is commendable.

Departure Scene: Among the Chinese participants were Ma Fengrui, Zhou Yuyu, and Dong Jia et al., a total of six people. In this participation, a total of 44 people. At 10 o'clock, they lined up in front of the Hongkou Park gate, and Pearce gave the order to start, heading towards Jiangwan Road. Verdun immediately took the lead, followed closely by Sgott, a soldier of the German army. Remy and Ma Fengrui followed together, and Nuggepot followed.

Flying Forward: After about a mile, they reached the wilderness. Verdun ran faster and faster, with tighter steps. Except for Remy and Ma Fengrui, all the rest fell far behind. After three miles, Verdun, Remy, and Ma were sixty or seventy yards ahead of the others. The situation changed half a mile from the finish line.

Ma Falls Behind: After crossing the Jiangwan Road Bridge, Verdun rushed forward. Remy and Ma tried desperately to catch up for two hundred yards. Ma Fengrui was exhausted and fell behind. Remy also tried hard to keep up, but ultimately felt no match for Verdun.

Swift Victory: Verdun still had plenty of energy, took the lead, and won the championship with a time of 44 minutes and 45 seconds, which was slightly worse than Remy's time last year, but the wind was quite strong, which was the reason for the inferiority. Remy was twenty-five yards behind, and Ma Fengrui was two hundred yards behind. After the race, Miss Hentou awarded the prizes.

Shanghai Coal Industry Proposes Recovering Kailuan Coal Mine 117

The Shanghai Coal Industry Association sent telegrams to the Nanjing Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters, and the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, stating: "The world's material evolution requires coal as a driving force in everything. The use of coal can be said to be grand. The relationship between coal and the prosperity and decline of the country is also extremely close. On February 19, 1910, British merchant Moller and Bime Company used fraudulent means to acquire the property of the Kaiping Mining Bureau without our side receiving any compensation. The perpetrators and destroyers in this matter were Zhang Yanmou, the director of the Kaiping Bureau, and Detring, the customs officer of Tianjin Hai Customs, who was the acting general manager of Kaiping. Although the Qing court later ordered Zhang Yanmou to recover the mine, Zhang Yanmou went to England to sue, which was justified in law, but in reality, he was still unable to recover it. This is a major and painful history of China's coal mines. During the Guangxu period, Zhou Xuexi raised funds to establish the Zhengzhou Coal Mine to resist Kaiping. However, due to weak capital and oppression from Kaiping, it was eventually merged by Kaiping, backfiring and causing heartache. This is the origin of the Kai Zheng Mining Bureau. For thirty years since then, the rights of the Kai Zheng Coal Mine have been in the hands of British merchants. Chinese shareholders receive only a small fraction of the profits. Their monopoly and manipulation have gone unquestioned. The losses in this matter are incalculable. We have always believed that all of China's humiliating and rights-compromising matters are caused by unequal treaties. Few know that the Kaiping Mining Bureau was cheated out of its property by British merchant Moller and Bime Company without compensation. Few also know that the Zhengzhou Coal Mine was annexed by British merchant Moller et al. through oppressive means. It can be said that the loss of the Kai Zheng Coal Mine does not fall within the scope of unequal treaties, but is due to the British merchants' use of illegal means, fraud, and annexation. If we say that canceling all unequal treaties will allow us to recover the Kai Zheng Coal Mine, it seems that this cannot be fully encompassed. This should be handled as a separate case, with legal action taken, and an audit of assets and compensation for damages sought in order to protect legal interests to the greatest extent possible. Now that the National Assembly is approaching, we respectfully submit this outline and request that the National Assembly allow the recovery of the Kai Zheng Coal Mine to be included on the agenda and discussed as a separate case. We hope to obtain appropriate methods and quickly set a recovery period in order to extend the spirit of the rule of law and rectify the country's coal rights. We earnestly submit this matter and pray for your approval. The country will be fortunate, the coal industry will be fortunate. The Shanghai Coal Industry Association respectfully submits."

China-Siam Communication Awaiting Ministry Order 122

Trial Reports Show Good Results

Due to the inability to directly communicate between China and Siam, international telegrams from the International Wireless Radio Telegraph Station established by the Ministry of Communications were forwarded by the Java Radio Station. Recently, the station deemed it necessary to directly transmit messages due to the close proximity between China and Siam. It then made preparations for trial broadcasts at the Fenglinqiao receiving station and the Liuhang transmitting station, and repeatedly conducted trial broadcasts with the ksg station established by the Siamese Radio Station. The radio waves were clear and fully capable of direct communication. The Ministry of Communications is currently in telegraphic communication with the Siamese government to discuss and finalize the China-Siam communication contract, which will be completed soon. As soon as the station receives instructions from the Ministry, it will officially begin communication.

Special News from the Shipping Industry 123

All Yangtze River Ships Resume Service: Since the Northern Expedition, Shanghai's Chinese-owned Yangtze River ships have been unable to fully resume service due to continuous warfare and the requisitioning of Yangtze River ships for military transport. In recent years, the Yangtze River shipping operations of China Merchants, Sanbei, and Ningshao have suffered significant losses. In order to consider the shipping merchants, the headquarters has given preferential lease payments for chartered ships and approved the issuance of shipping bonds to subsidize them. Now that military transport has ended, the Yangtze River ships of the three companies are being gradually released by the Ministry of Communications. China Merchants and Sanbei have resumed operations with the released ships in recent days. Ningshao's Yongxing ship, the last to be released to Shanghai, will also arrive in Shanghai today. After entering the dock for repairs, it will join the Yangtze River route. The Yangtze River Chinese ships, which have been out of service for several years, will be fully operational from today.

Request to Abolish Inner Harbor Licenses: The Jianghai Customs has promulgated regulations on the licensing of commercial ships in the inner harbor, notifying various shipping companies in Shanghai to promptly have their ships operating in the inner harbor re-licensed. After discussions among the shipping merchants in Shanghai, it was unanimously agreed that the customs' establishment of inner harbor ship licenses was intended to restrict foreign ships. If Chinese commercial ships have already complied with regulations and presented their registration to the Ministry and obtained a customs ship license, they should not be required to re-license their inner harbor ships, as this would be self-restricting. This matter was raised at the transportation conference and was passed but not implemented. The entire Shanghai shipping merchants association should submit a request to the Ministry, ordering all customs houses to immediately abolish the unfavorable regulations requiring Chinese commercial ships to re-license their inner harbor ships. The Shipping Association has now been publicly elected to submit a request to the Ministry to abolish this regulation.

Weihai Route Opens: After British ships abandoned the Weihaiwei route, the China Merchants Bureau proposed taking over the route. Xu Zushan of the Weihaiwei Administration also repeatedly requested the bureau to send ships to operate the route to facilitate cargo, passengers, and mail, thereby boosting the market. The China Merchants Bureau accepted his request and, following the example of British ships, requested the Ministry of Communications to allocate 4,000 yuan to the bureau. This case has been under negotiation for a long time and has not yet been approved, and the Weihai Administration has also failed to commit to payment. The China Merchants Bureau has now drafted regulations for adding the Weihai Bureau, and has signed a contract with the Weihai manager in charge, stipulating 18 articles. It is agreed that expenses will be deducted from the freight charges. A certain amount of expenses will be given for each ship. Once the contract is signed, the Beiyang ship will be ordered to also serve Weihai. Since the subsidy has not been received, a temporary agency will be established, and it will be expanded into a branch office once business develops.

Railroad Materials Transported to Hankou: A large batch of railroad tracks newly purchased from the United Kingdom by the Pinghan Railway has arrived, totaling 500 tons. New materials for the Yellow River Railway Bridge have also arrived at the same time. This cargo has been temporarily unloaded at the Yunzaobang Wharf in Wusong. Because of the urgent need to load it for laying, the Ministry of Railways has agreed with the British merchant Taikoo Shipping (Chinese commercial ships do not have heavy lifting equipment and cannot transport it, so foreign ships have been converted) to transport the railroad tracks and new bridges from Wusong to Hankou for laying.

Fourth Day Diary of the Chinese Medical and Pharmaceutical Congress 126

Yesterday (the 6th) was the fourth day of the Chinese Medical and Pharmaceutical Society's conference. From 9 a.m., academic lectures continued, chaired alternately by Da Wang and Qu Shaoheng. Guest lecturers included Professor Kondo from Japan, who presented an outline of his research on morphine clusters, translated by Zeng Guangfang. Member lecturers included Zhou Mengbai, who reviewed the Chinese Pharmacopoeia; Yang Yujie, who discussed the prevalence of cholera in Shanghai; Tao Lie, who spoke on the function of the central nervous system; Tao Chison, who discussed the phonetic curves of the Chinese language; and Wu Zhi, who discussed the treatment of epidemic cerebrospinal meningitis. From 1 p.m. to 2 p.m., medical films were screened, totaling three reels: (1) Lumbar puncture, (2) Skull and brain surgery, and (3) Normal delivery. Lectures continued from 2 p.m., chaired alternately by Gu Yuesa and He Zhidong. Guest lecturers included Professor Hiramitsu Goichi from Japan, who spoke on the research of Japanese brains relating to East Asians, translated by Tao Chison, and Professor Zhu Hengbi from the Central Medical College, who discussed the research of sheep flower toxin. Member lecturers included Yang Ziqian, who discussed the hemolytic effect of tiger-la bacteria, etc. The lectures stopped around 4 p.m., and the articles of association and various branch proposals were discussed, chaired by Chen Fangzhi. After passing the articles of association, the proposals were discussed, divided into six categories: association affairs, academics, medical administration, medical education, pharmaceuticals, and careers, totaling forty-one items. Due to time constraints, the results were left for discussion today. At 6 p.m. in the evening, a public banquet was held by the pharmaceutical department of Baibu Foreign Company, and from 8 p.m. to 10 p.m., popular hygiene lectures continued, presented by Chen Fangzhi, Cai Yumen, Zhang Zitai, Tang Juexian, etc. Lectures will continue today from 9 a.m. to 3 p.m., and after 3 p.m., the articles of association will be discussed and officers re-elected, it is said.

Preparation of the Kaicheng Acid Manufacturing Plant Completed 128

Groundbreaking on the 10th of This Month, Delivery on National Day

More than ten people, including Xu Xian, Xiang Songmao, Fang Yexian, Lin Dian, Yu Qiaqing, and Yu Heqin, in view of the fact that the basic raw materials of China's chemical industry are supplied by others and are often subject to restrictions, Mr. Fu Chun initiated the Kaicheng Acid Manufacturing Joint-Stock Limited Company, which set up a factory in Shanghai to manufacture sulfuric, nitric, and hydrochloric acid to meet the urgent needs of domestic chemical plants. After being approved by the military, political, industrial, and commercial departments, chemical engineers Lin Dazhong, Gao Xian, and Fang Luxi, accountant Yu Zhongwang, and architectural engineer Wang Kesheng were hired for planning and design. Everything is now ready. The groundbreaking ceremony was held on the 4th of this month at the factory site outside Jungong Road, and construction will begin on the 10th to build the factory buildings. The entire project is contracted by Xi Zhiji and is scheduled to be completed by the end of July. The machinery will then be manufactured, and delivery is expected on National Day. It is also heard that when construction begins on the 10th, Mayor Zhang is expected to attend the groundbreaking ceremony to show his importance, it is said.

Negotiation of Road Repair Across the Border 129

The Hongqiao Road, built by the Shanghai West of Border area, has recently had the British Public Works Bureau send people to repair the road. This has been discovered by the Municipal Public Utility Bureau, which believes that the road is located in the Chinese territory and foreigners should not overstep their authority. Japanese Ship Sinking Chinese Ship Case 130

The Ministry of Foreign Affairs Orders the Nagasaki Consul to Negotiate

According to news from the Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Shanghai, regarding the incident of the Japanese ship "Himeshima Maru" sinking the ship of Zhu Aliang, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs had ordered the consul in Nagasaki to earnestly negotiate with the ship's company, the Kihira Joint-Stock Company, and order them to compensate Zhu Aliang for all losses. The Kihira Company used the excuse that the ships collided and both parties suffered losses, and that it would only be able to fulfill its obligations after the Admiralty Court made a ruling based on the facts. Now, a telegram has been received from the consul in Nagasaki stating that the case has been determined by the Admiralty Court to not require a trial, so the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has sent a telegram ordering the consul to continue negotiating with the Kihira Company. The report that the Office ordered Zhu to file a lawsuit with the Japanese consulate is not factual.

Japanese Stealing Photos of Forts 131

The Fortress Headquarters Sends a Letter Requesting the Municipal Government to Negotiate

Yan Zemin, the commander of the guard of the Wusong District Fortress Headquarters, reported a few days ago that several foreigners wearing Western clothes suddenly came to the rear guard post of the headquarters, carrying cameras, and secretly photographed the South Fort of the fortress. Commander Yan believed that this matter concerned foreigners spying on China's national defense secrets, so he immediately led the guards,

Fortress, foreigners are not allowed to take pictures without authorization, in order to attach importance to national defense and promote friendly relations, and temporarily detained the two cameras carried by the Japanese and turned them over to the department. The deputy adjutant of the department, Shen Zitian, together with Mr. Yan and others, went to the site to investigate and found that the foreigners were still lingering. It was learned that they were all Japanese nationals, named Yoshitomi Yoshiki, Otsuki Shun, Kaii Yowao, and Obata Kenkichi, all employees of the Nichihua Textile Co., Ltd., currently residing at 98 Robert Road. They claimed that they came to Songjiang this time purely for a spring outing, and took photos of the fort only because of its beautiful scenery, and had no other intentions. They took out a stack of banknotes from their pockets and tried to bribe Deputy Adjutant Shen, asking for the return of the cameras. Deputy Adjutant Shen strictly refused, saying that this matter was of great importance and must be reported to the superiors for handling, and that he had no authority to handle it. The four Japanese then remained silent and left. Later, the sentry reported that there were seven or eight Japanese in total that day, carrying no less than five or six cameras. After the guard commander Yan Zemin stopped them, four or five people took the opportunity to escape, so only these four people were left. The photos reflected in the cameras were all torn up by the Japanese on the spot. However, these broken photos have now been collected and presented to the department by Mr. Yan. Deng Zhenquan, commander of the Wusong District Fortress, believed that this matter was of great importance, so he sent a letter to the Municipal Government detailing the incident, requesting that the Municipal Government forward the letter to the Japanese Consul General in Shanghai to punish the Japanese and ensure that this type of incident does not happen again in the future. It is learned that the Municipal Government has already sent a letter to the Japanese Consul General in Shanghai, Murai Kuramatsu, requesting that he promptly comply, it is said.

Customs Workers Strike Yesterday 135

Opposing the Cotton Cloth Industry Association's Cancellation of Transportation Fees

More than 800 customs workers in this city went on strike yesterday morning because the Cotton Cloth Industry Association implemented the cancellation of cotton cloth transportation fees and customs inspection fees, and repeated requests to restore them were unsuccessful. The details are as follows: Yesterday's Strike Customs workers have been paid transportation fees and customs inspection fees by merchants dealing in cotton cloth for more than eighty years. Now, the Cotton Cloth Industry Association has decided that, starting from April 1st, buyers will be responsible for these fees themselves. Repeated requests to restore the original transportation fees have not been adequately answered by the Association, so they automatically went on strike yesterday morning. However, workers were still sent to clear customs for foreign miscellaneous goods.

Organizing Inspection Teams After the customs workers went on strike, in order to prevent smuggling, they organized inspection teams, divided into day and night shifts. There were a total of thirteen day teams: (1) Checking stack manifests at various foreign firms, Cheng Pinshun, Jiang Miaojin; (2) Customs and Revenue and Taxation Bureau, Yu Xingfa; (3) Mitsubishi Wharf to Huashun Wharf, Tian Sichao, Shui Yulong; (4) Yangshupu Factory to Sanxin Factory, Gu Haibao, Cheng Xiankang; (5) Shanghai Factory to Donghua Factory, Tian Qiru, Wang Shusheng; (6) Santai to Gongda Factory, Wang Dagen, Feng Jiulin; (7) Warehouse to Hengfeng Factory, Xu Shenggui, Zhu Jinquan; (8) Zhentai Factory to Shenxin No. 2 Factory, Ni Zipeng, Ying Bingxin; (9) Inside and Outside Thirteen Factories to Gongyi Factory, Yu Yueyou, Mei Rulin; (10) Da Wang Temple to Inside and Outside Nine Factories, Shen Linde, Yan Hen; (11) Puyi No. 2 Factory to Inside and Outside No. 3 Factory, Wang Gentang, Wan Kunlin; (12) Lihe Stack to Fengji Stack, Wu Xinhua, Wang Ruisheng; (13) Ewo Wharf to Huangpu Wharf, Jiang Ansheng, Liang Jihe. There were a total of five night teams: (1) Taikoo Wharf to Hongan Wharf, Lu Pinhua; (2) Dada Wharf to Ning Shao Wharf, Chen Pinjin; (3) Mitsubishi Wharf to Tonghua Shun Wharf, Lu Hongshou; (4) Huishan Wharf to Huangpu Wharf, Zhang Yusun; (5) Longmao Stack, Shen Ziguang. The inspection was carried out day and night, and there were no cases of smuggling. The order after the strike was good.

Authorities Investigating Customs clearance has always been responsible for reporting Chinese and foreign cotton yarn, cloth, and foreign miscellaneous goods. If it were to completely stop, ships would inevitably have no goods to load, which would have a significant impact on transportation. In view of this, the Municipal Society immediately sent Zhang Shuye to investigate the truth and report it so that it could be verified and handled.

The Labor Union Presents a Document The Customs Industry Union yesterday presented a document to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, stating that the Cotton Cloth Industry Association's covenant is forcibly deducting transportation fees and inspection fees. They request that you examine and verify the matter and promptly and strictly stop it. Since March 10th, members of the union have reported to the union that the Cotton Cloth Industry Association has discontinued the payment of transportation fees, etc., which have been earned through the blood and sweat of the members for decades, since February 21st of the national calendar. After receiving the news, the union immediately convened a meeting of all directors and supervisors on March 15th and decided to first inquire about the facts. After a week, there was no reply, so they sent a letter urging a clear response. However, the association ignored it. The union was preparing to send representatives to the association to inquire about the situation, but the members rushed to the union, demanding prompt action. Therefore, the union respectfully presented a document, inviting your bureau to send personnel to the union on April 4th for guidance. However, before another day could pass, the Cotton Cloth Industry Association finally announced the release of all the union's inherent benefits in the Xin Shen and Liang newspapers on April 3rd. How can the members of the union support their families with such a small amount of hard work? Usually, they rely on transportation fees, etc., to help them with their livelihood. Moreover, this subsidy is paid by the sellers, not by the Cotton Cloth Industry Association, and it is not an excessive request by the union members. Now, the association has suddenly come up with this deceitful plan to enrich itself and monopolize the market. What is the conscience of the association when the livelihood of more than 800 members of the union is at stake? At a time when the cost of living is rising day by day, they are afraid that they will not have enough time to work hard. How can the economy withstand further stimulation? The union cannot help but feel disheartened by the reports in the newspapers. Therefore, at the general assembly of representatives on the 4th, there was hardly any space left for the members who attended. The workers at the entire venue requested to go on strike immediately. Comrade Zhang Shuye, a special commissioner of your bureau, and the directors of the union, did not agree to the request, advocating for prudent handling and waiting for a solution. Unfortunately, the noise of the crowd could not be stopped. The members then put forward two conditions: (1) that the matter be resolved in the shortest possible time; (2) that all expenses be fully paid by the union until the matter is resolved, otherwise they will take free action. The directors of the union were afraid of expanding the unrest, so they had to submit a document and respectfully request your bureau to convene both parties for mediation as soon as possible.

Hat Workers Strike 136

Opposing the Employer's Excessive Recruitment of Apprentices

More than 400 hat workers in this city went on strike on April 5th because employers were excessively recruiting apprentices, resulting in unemployed workers who had no way to find employment and deducting workers' wages, making it impossible for them to maintain their daily lives. After the labor union sent representatives to negotiate with the responsible representatives of the industry association without success, they went on strike automatically to prompt the employers to realize their mistakes. Yesterday morning, Changwang Yuxiang and others, the permanent directors of the labor union, went to the Social Affairs Bureau to petition and issued a declaration requesting assistance from all sectors and presenting it to the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Civil Training Committee, and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, requesting a speedy mediation, it is said.

Jinxin Silk Weaving Factory Strike 137

The Jinxin Silk Weaving Factory on Sassoon Road in the French Concession has been on strike for several weeks. Although the Social Affairs Bureau has taken the initiative to mediate, the employer has never attended. Yesterday morning at 9:00, the mediation period arrived again, and the employer still insisted on everything, leaving no room for negotiation, so it ended without results. Last night at 8:00, the labor union convened a general assembly of all members, and it was heard that the Social Affairs Bureau and the workers would jointly submit a request to the Municipal Government for arbitration to resolve everything, it is said.

Limited to Before April 30th

The Land Bureau Will Provide Prices According to Regulations

The plan to open the western section of Heping Road (i.e., Ximen Road) and renovate the road surface in the old Ximen area has long been drafted by the Public Works Bureau and submitted to the Municipal Government for approval. Bureau Chief Shen Yi believes that this project is of great importance to the Shanghai South market and east-west traffic and should be built as soon as possible. Therefore, he will jointly issue a notice with the Land Bureau to the residents of the area, requiring all houses obstructing the road to be demolished and cleared by April 30th to facilitate construction. The Land Bureau will recover the land at a price according to the regulations on road construction and fee collection. If the demolition is not completed by the deadline, the Public Works Bureau and the Land Bureau will enforce it, it is said.

Business Licenses Still Need to Have Stamps Affixed 140

The Jiangsu Shangbao Stamp Tax Bureau sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating that various provinces are preparing business taxes, and in the future, all stores should apply for business licenses. The stamps that should be affixed to the licenses have been stipulated by the Ministry of Finance: those with capital of more than 500 yuan should affix a 5-jiao stamp tax ticket, and those with capital of less than 500 yuan should affix a 1-jiao stamp tax ticket. Please forward this to the industry associations for reference.

Revision of the Postal Fee List 141

According to Shanghai postal circles, several items in the Postal Fee List No. 70 have been revised, as follows: (D) Insured Letters: In addition to the ordinary postage and registration fee, an insurance fee of 2 jiao will be charged for every 240 yuan insured or any odd amount. The maximum amount of insurance is 2,000 yuan in silver dollars. (E) Insured Boxes: In addition to the ordinary postage of 1 jiao 6 fen for every fifty centimeters, (postage starts at 8 jiao) and the domestic registration fee, an insurance fee of 2 jiao will be charged for every 240 yuan insured or any odd amount. The maximum amount of insurance is 2,000 yuan in silver dollars. (G) Parcel Insurance Fee: For an insured amount not exceeding 240 yuan in silver dollars, the fee is 4 jiao. For every 240 yuan insured or any odd amount, an additional fee of 2 jiao is charged.

Local News Two

Pacification of the Sea off Songkou 151

Recently, the sea around Wusongkou has been restless. Although fishing boats are ready, they still dare not go out to sea. The provincial government believes that the spring fishing season is not only the biggest business for fishermen and merchants, but also greatly related to national tax revenue. Therefore, it has joined forces with the Pacification Commissioner and the Navy Department to carry out a major suppression. A temporary Zeng Office was established outside Songkou. Yesterday, a fleet led by the commissioner set off to suppress pirates in the Lvsi sea area, with a deadline to completely clear them out before the Grain Rain solar term, so that fishing boats can go out to sea to catch fish, maintain the fishing season, and increase tax revenue.

Opening of Longhua Temple 152

Longhua Temple, located in the southwestern suburbs of this city, is a famous ancient temple in Shanghai. It is said to have been built in the tenth year of Chiwu during the Three Kingdoms period, more than 2,000 years ago. The temple has a Sutra Repository with more than 10,000 volumes of scriptures and a bronze Buddha from the Jin Dynasty, all of which are inherited relics. Next to it is a seven-story pagoda built during the Tang Dynasty's Guanzong era. To the west of the temple is a memorial tower for the soldiers who died in the 32nd Army. At this time of bright spring, with peach blossoms and green willows, tourists come and go, almost like on the Shanyin Road. The abbot of the temple, Yuanzhao, has ordered craftsmen to renovate all the Buddha halls and display the calligraphy and paintings of famous people from past dynasties for people to view. It has been fully opened since the day before yesterday. The Shanghai South Public Bus Company has also added special buses to travel between Old Ximen and Longhua.

The Dispute Involving the Shanghai South Public Bus Yesterday 153

The Company Asks the Authorities to Protect the Service

The Defense Corps Sent Personnel Yesterday to Investigate Thoroughly

The details of the incident in which the ticket collector of the Shanghai South Public Bus Company's Route 2 special bus to Longhua was beaten by the Longhua First Team of the Caohejing Defense Corps police have been reported in yesterday's newspaper. The company believes that this matter should be mediated by the Public Security Bureau and the Public Utilities Bureau. Yesterday, it specifically requested the two bureaus to send teams to protect the operation of the Route 2 bus to Longhua, to avoid further accidents. The following is the original text of the bus company's report to the Public Utilities Bureau and the Public Security Bureau:

Reporting Matter: On the 5th of this month, at 4:00 PM, the ticket collector Ni Wuyi reported that while he was serving on Special Bus No. 19, the bus arrived at Longhua, and suddenly, Gao Diankui, the squad leader of the Longhua First Team of the Caohejing District Defense Corps, led more than 20 militiamen, including Zhu Shiyuan, rushing up. Wei Zixin, fearing a conflict, immediately ordered the bus to be changed to a regular bus and depart. Only one person bought a two-cent ticket, seven people bought three-cent tickets, and the rest refused to buy tickets. When the bus arrived at Maogong Bridge, they rushed off, intending to ask the driver Xu Aliang to turn back to Longhua to pick up passengers. However, Gao Diankui and others, having been instigated by the Captain Wu Rugui, refused to allow the bus to turn around, dragged the reporter down, causing injuries to his waist and feet, destroyed his hat and uniform, and snatched his copper badge. They remained by the bridge, not allowing him to report to the police station. He had to return to the company to report. The ticket collector Wang Hengxi reported that while he was serving on Special Bus No. 15, traveling from Ximen to Maogong Bridge, he was stopped by more than 20 members of the Longhua Defense Corps in Caohejing District, who boarded the bus and occupied the passenger seats, not allowing passengers to board. Despite people's persuasion, the ticket collector Xue Xianglin reported that while he was serving on the special bus, going down to Maogong Bridge, he was stopped by more than 20 members of the Defense Corps, who forcibly boarded the bus without buying tickets and slapped him in the face. He had reported to the police station. Captain Jia led the police to persuade them. The driver Zhang Qiankun reported that while he was serving on the regular bus, going down to Maogong Bridge, because the bus was full, the more than 20 members of the Defense Corps blocked the bus from stopping. Then squad leader Gao led the members to chase after him on a regular bus going off duty, trying to snatch his hat. The police dispersed them. One after another, the two routes were obstructed, and the situation was extremely tense. He immediately instructed the external affairs personnel to transfer the cars stranded at Ximen back to Route 3. On one side, Director Yang Pingcai and Xia Shuxiang followed Director Liu of the Sixth District Office's phone call and met with him. Director Zhang of the Public Security Bureau and Engineer An of the Public Utilities Bureau were also present, and the above situations were reported separately. It was found that the Defense Corps was established to protect merchants and civilians, and is under the jurisdiction of the Municipal Government. Wu Rugui is the captain, he should abide by the law and restrain his subordinates. However, because of the reduction in fares, after external affairs personnel discovered and reported it, they followed the Public Utilities Bureau's order No. 1197 to make up the tickets. Suddenly, on the afternoon of this day, taking advantage of the large number of passengers, he ordered Squad Leader Gao Diankui of the team to lead more than 20 militiamen, repeatedly ordering the special bus, which was approved not to stop along the way, to pick up and drop off passengers at Maogong Bridge Station, violating the rules, and violently beating the driver and ticket collector. This obstructs traffic, and they are willing to test the law with their own bodies. In addition to following the instructions of Director Zhang and Engineer An to resume traffic and reporting to the Public Security Bureau and Public Utilities Bureau, this document is submitted to your bureaus for review and forwarding to the Municipal Government, ordering the Shanghai South District Defense Corps Reorganization Committee to first suspend Wu Rugui and others from their duties and send them to the court for punishment according to law, in order to ensure the safety of business. The urgency of waiting for orders is beyond words. Sincerely submitted to Chen, the Director of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, and Huang, the Director of the Public Utilities Bureau, Shanghai South Public Bus Co., Ltd.

The Municipal Defense Corps Reorganization Committee believes that the details of the Shanghai South Public Bus incident must be investigated clearly before a thorough investigation can be conducted. Committee Chairman Sun Baorong ordered Wang Zhuangfei, the Deputy Commander of the Shanghai South District Defense Corps, and Fan Ju, the Chief Instructor, to go to investigate the details of the incident yesterday. Wang and Fan went to various places to investigate yesterday. However, according to the Caohejing Defense Corps, the report in the newspaper was a misunderstanding. At that time, more than 30 members of the team were all armed and took the bus from Longhua to Shanghai. Although many people wanted to board the bus, the team members said that the bus was limited to 30 passengers by the Public Utilities Bureau, fearing that it would exceed the quota and cause danger due to the small bus and many people. Therefore, they immediately instructed the bus to depart. When the bus arrived at Maogong Bridge, some of the team members got off, while others still intended to go to Shanghai. The driver and ticket collector insisted on turning back to Longhua. The team members were afraid that they would not have enough time, so they fought each other, causing a conflict. This was the actual situation at the time of the incident. After receiving the report, Wang and Fan went to the Second Office of the Sixth District to investigate the details of the incident and learned the details. However, the Public Bus Company and the Defense Corps each held their own views. The two immediately made a detailed report on the information obtained from the investigations and submitted it to Chairman Sun for review, in order to conduct a thorough investigation. It is heard that the Public Bus Company has also submitted a report to the Public Utilities Bureau, requesting strict negotiations.

Taihu Bandit Chief Tai Bao A Shu Captured 154

Extremely Vicious When Arrested

Savagely Bit the Finger of Detective Gu

His Brother Has Also Been Arrested

Will Be Sent to the Security Team for Review

When the second leader of the Taihu bandits, Sha Zhu Luo A Mei, was arrested in Shanghai on the 25th of last month, information was obtained at the same time that the escaped bandit chief Tai Bao A Shu Xu Tianxiong had also sneaked into Shanghai and was hiding in a rented house near the North Railway Station in the Chinese territory owned by the Qian family. At that time, there were already informants tracking him, and they immediately reported to the First District of the Minhang Jiangsu Provincial Maritime Public Security Team. Director Xu, upon receiving the report, immediately ordered Fan Guozhong, the captain of the First Team, to secretly bring more than ten detectives to Shanghai to arrest him. When they arrived near the North Railway Station to ambush him, Xu had already heard the news and escaped an hour earlier. An inspection of all the furnishings in the house showed that they had not been moved, and it was assumed that he must have fled to the Concession. Therefore, a strict search was carried out. Until two days ago, it was discovered that Xu and his brother Fusheng were indeed together in Shanghai, and temporarily used the Huide Lane, Dalian Bay Road, and Huaiyuan Lane as places for contact and communication. Therefore, at around 12:00 noon the day before yesterday, all the detectives gathered at the entrance of the lane to wait. Not long after, Xu swaggered over and was arrested. However, during the arrest, Detective Gu Lansheng's left middle finger and ring finger were savagely bitten by the bandit, almost to the point of being bitten off. He was immediately taken to the Huishan Police Station. After a detailed interrogation by the chief of police, the bandit directly admitted that over the years, he had gathered more than 2,000 followers and repeatedly looted villages and towns in Jin, Ping, Song, Jia, and other places, kidnapped people for ransom, and joined the Red Bandits. He was even falsely appointed by Yan Xishan to disrupt the rear of the National Army and instigate the assassination of maritime detective Sun Huanwen at No. 10 Baoyu Lane in the French Concession. He also confessed that his brother Fusheng was currently hiding in the Central Apartment on Avenue Edward VII. Therefore, the original detectives went to the address and arrested Fusheng. It is heard that they will be transferred to the Second Regiment of the Songjiang Jiangsu Provincial Security Team for review and dealt with together with Sha Zhu Luo A Mei.

According to someone from Songjiang, the news of the arrest of Tai Bao A Shu Xu Tianxiong, the leader of the lake bandits who roamed the four counties of Songjiang, Jinshan, Pinghu, and Jiading, was reported to the Songjiang County Government on the evening of the 5th by Detective Fei Guanqing of the First Team of the Water Police, stating that he had been captured at the entrance of Huiyuanfang, Huade Road, Hongkou, Shanghai, and was now in the Huishan Police Station. After the formalities were completed, he could be sent to Songjiang, etc. According to the detectives who participated in the arrest, Captain Fan Guozhong of the First Team of the Second District of the Water Police, based on a report from a secret agent, after the arrest of Zhu Luo A Mei, Tai Bao A Shu and others were organizing an organization in the Huade Road area, but the location of the building number was not known. Captain Fan immediately gave travel expenses to those who knew Tai Bao A Shu and sent them to Huade Road to rent a room on the first floor of Huiyuanfang, with a window facing the road, where pedestrians could be seen. They stayed there to observe. Sure enough, at around 12:00 noon on the 5th, Gu Lansheng saw Tai Bao A Shu walking on the road, and realized that the time had come. He immediately exchanged glances with the detectives ambushing at the entrance of the lane. Gu Lansheng directly called out his name, asked him where he was going, and went up to arrest him. A Shu fiercely bit Gu's finger. Gu endured the pain and refused to let go, calling for more people to surround him. The police heard the sound and rushed over. Tai Bao A Shu tried to bribe the police with the banknotes he had on him, but the Western police had already arrived, so he was taken to the Huishan Police Station. At this point, Tai Bao A Shu's attitude became calm. He asked the police for tea and dishes. During the interrogation, he confessed that he was 29 years old, from Liujia Yanqiao, Jinshan. In the past, he was appointed by Yan and Feng to disrupt the rear. If they had not failed, we would all be in important positions. On the 14th of the first month, he disguised himself as a villager and broke out of the encirclement. After smoking opium at Jinshanwei, he hired a sampan and went by sea to Bailonggang to land, took a long-distance bus to Shanghai, and asked where his residence in Shanghai was. He said that he had a wife everywhere, so he had a home everywhere. Now that I have been arrested, what is the point of asking about my home? Then, Director Xu and Captain Fan Guozhong asked him if he had paid someone to assassinate us. He replied that it might have happened, and said that this place was just a temporary residence and there was no need to ask in detail. The maritime detective also learned that Tai Bao A Shu's brother, Xu Fusheng, was suffering from inguinal lymphadenitis and was hiding in the Central Apartment on Avenue Edward VII. Therefore, they went to arrest him and learned where the guns were hidden. In addition to sending people to the location he provided to seize the weapons, Director Xu and others planned to bring him back to the case. It is heard that the detectives who were guarding the scene included Fei Guanqing, Gu Lansheng, Gu Chungeng, Chen Long, etc. After receiving the news here, it is rumored that he will be sent to Songjiang today. Many citizens traveling between the railway station and the wharf hope to see the bandit's face, but it is said that he must first go to the Minhang District Department before he can be sent to Songjiang, so it will not be until tomorrow or the day after tomorrow. The bandit leader has been captured, and everyone believes that the day when the bandit scourge will be eliminated is not far away, which is truly a great relief.

Shanghai News of Mr. Ma Su's Death 155

Mr. Ma Su, also known as Suwu, the current Senior Advisor to the Deputy Commander-in-Chief of the National Government's Army, Navy, and Air Force, passed away at his residence in Beijing on the evening of the 4th due to overwork and illness. When the sad news came, everyone mourned. Mr. Ma was born in Guangzhou in 1883. He studied in the United States at New York University. After completing his studies, he followed Premier Sun to assist in the revolutionary cause. In the first year of the Republic of China, he served as the Western Secretary of the Nanjing Provisional Government. During the Second Revolution, he was ordered by the Premier to found newspapers such as the China Republican to promote justice and strongly attack the monarchy, which led to the closure of the newspaper by Yuan Shikai, and Mr. Ma was sent abroad. In the United States, he served as the Minister of the American Headquarters of the Kuomintang. When the Guangzhou Extraordinary President was established, he was sent to the United States as a special envoy for foreign affairs and a commercial commissioner. During the Pacific Conference, he served as the plenipotentiary representative of the South. Later, when the Premier served as the Commander-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force, preparing for the Northern Expedition, he recruited Mr. Ma back to China to serve as the Secretary of the General Headquarters and Director of External Publicity. When he saw Borodin holding the party affairs and spreading communism, he was one of the first opponents. Not being able to achieve his goals, he traveled in Europe and the United States. Columbia University in the United States hired him as a professor of Chinese. After national unification, the Commander of the Northeast Border Defense Division hired him for his current position.

Reduction of Delays on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway 157

Many Effective Dispatching Methods

Recently, the Beijing-Shanghai Railway has been experiencing delays due to old locomotives. Therefore, Pacific locomotives have been purchased to improve the situation. First, the Traffic Department ordered the Dispatching Section to carefully study and revise the timetable in consultation with the heads of various Traffic Sections. It has been implemented since April 1. Since the implementation of the new timetable, the speed of the special express trains has increased, the time has been shortened, and there have been fewer delays. Even the slow third and fourth-class trains, which have been delayed for a long time in the past, can arrive on time. It is also heard that the new timetable is very well-arranged, the trains on the way are staggered, and the timing is consistent, so the delays of the trains can be reduced. Moreover, according to the time of each train arranged this time, there is a leading train. If it is delayed for some reason, the following train will never overtake it midway, which can meet the needs of travelers. As for the allocation of locomotives, it is heard that the newly purchased Pacific locomotives will be used for the night special express trains, express trains, and third and fourth-class trains with more carriages, because this type of locomotive has a large towing force, which is very suitable for towing trains with more carriages. The other special express trains are towed by the original C and E-type locomotives with higher speeds, and the number of carriages is limited, so they can travel faster when carrying light loads. In addition, the railway is also making every effort to renovate the roadbed to increase the speed of the train without danger.
