Red Pill Organization Cracked Down on Haikou Road 165

In recent years, there have been more and more people selling red pills secretly in Shanghai. Because of their lower price than opium and their more potent medicinal properties, many smokers abandon opium and prefer red pills. In the future, the spread of their poisonous atmosphere will be even worse than the opium addiction. Although the police have strictly prohibited and investigated, it is difficult to eliminate them. The area around Six Malu has almost become a market for the secret production and sale of red pills. There have been several crackdowns in the past, and these people have become a little more restrained. However, recently they have returned to their original state. The day before yesterday, the Old Zha Police Station secretly dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to House No. 6 on Haikou Road and discovered a red pill manufacturing organization. They seized 127 large and small packages of red pills, along with Wu Amao from Suzhou and Yao Amao from Jiancheng who were selling them. They were detained and sent to the District Court for prosecution in the morning, requesting severe punishment in accordance with Articles 6 and 13 of the Opium Prohibition Law. The defendants Wu and Yao also confessed without denial. Judge Zhou sentenced Wu, the leader, to one year of imprisonment and a fine of 120 yuan. Yao, the helper, was sentenced to six months of imprisonment, and the red pills were confiscated.

Detective Lang also explained the process of solving the case, stating that the fourth defendant, Xiong Binglin, had taken off his old blue cloth robe and put on the stolen silk clothes after the robbery. The robbers packed the stolen goods in a white leather suitcase and hired a car to transport them. The stolen goods were presented as evidence. Judge Wu Tingqi verified the confessions, questioned the defendants briefly, and ordered them to be detained for further investigation at a later date.

Tragedy on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Train Line 167

Two Villagers, One Dead, One Injured

Yesterday afternoon, at approximately 1:10 PM, between Xujiahui and Xinlonghua, at the 14.5-kilometer mark on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, a villager of about thirty years of age was walking on the tracks. The early express train No. 35 from Zha Kou to Shanghai was approaching. The villager was unable to avoid the train in time and was crushed by the locomotive, resulting in immediate death. The conductor reported the incident to the stationmaster at Xujiahui, who dispatched police to investigate and notified the local bailiff to report to the court for an inquest. As the deceased had no family, the railway bureau provided 20 yuan for funeral expenses, and the bailiff prepared a coffin for burial.

Also, yesterday afternoon, at approximately 1:30 PM, the early express train No. 36 from Shanghai to Hangzhou was passing the 131-kilometer mark near Xieqiao when a villager of about forty years of age was walking in the area. The villager was struck by the locomotive, suffering injuries to the head, face, and lower body. Still faintly breathing, the villager was transported by police vehicle to a hospital in Hangzhou for treatment.

A Paper Listing Sworn Brothers Found in His Wallet

The incident was reported to prosecutor Yang of the local court, who arrived to conduct an inquest and determined that the death was due to illness. The body was entrusted to a charity for burial.

Special Article

Discussions on the New Salt Law in the Legislative Yuan - Zhang Peiyan 175

According to reports, the Legislative Yuan passed the Salt Law, consisting of seven chapters and thirty-nine articles, at its 136th meeting. I deeply understand that the Salt Law is of great importance to the national economy and the people's livelihood, and I dare not remain silent and complacent, leaving the country with an irreparable disaster. Therefore, I do not wish to engage in empty theoretical debates, but rather to point out the obstacles and defects in fact, to serve as a humble contribution for the authorities to consider. If it is possible to provide assistance in advance, to understand the true situation of salt administration, salt field production, sales, transportation, and storage in our country, to proceed cautiously, and not to apply rigid academic theories to the multifaceted salt affairs, then the Executive Yuan will not lose its dignity in the future, and the country and the people will be spared from danger. This matter concerns the governance of the Republic of China, and it is not to shield or lobby for one or two salt merchants. I earnestly hope that you gentlemen will carefully examine and analyze each article, listed as follows: (1) Salt should be taxed at the field, allowing people to buy and sell freely. The strongest advocate of this view in modern times is Zhang Jian of Nantong, who wrote "Opinions on Reforming the National Salt Law," and argued that for the sake of safeguarding the country and caring for the people, eliminating bandits, it is appropriate to change the salt law. He extensively discussed the adoption of Liu Yan's method of taxing at the field, hoping to achieve a situation where "the former merchant is still a merchant, and the former bandit is also a merchant," etc. When he was an outsider, holding a pen in his hand, he believed that he had thoroughly understood the past and present, grasping the beginning and the end, and found the treasure. He believed that

there was no better law than this. However, when he became a cabinet member in charge of salt administration, why did he not propose to implement it? Close examination of the facts reveals that this is because the ideal is not realistic. Various legal codes must be improved with each era. Liu Yan already implemented taxation at the field. If the law was truly good, then it should have been preserved and not replaced. Why did Wang Xianzhi and Huang Chao both gather crowds and rebel by selling illicit salt before the end of the Li Tang Dynasty? (See "Tang Ji Xizong Qianfu Second Year," note: Liu Yan's precise salt law began in the 14th year of Emperor Daizong's Dali reign and lasted only 95 years until the 2nd year of Emperor Xizong's Qianfu reign.) After the overthrow of the Tang Dynasty, the law was changed and implemented for more than 1,200 years (see Zhang Jian's "Yi Bian Yan Yi"). Although it is said that there is no law that does not become corrupt after a hundred years, the gains and losses, elimination of abuses, and patching of flaws have undergone countless processes. However, I have never heard of a fundamental law being changed because successive generations lacked people who understood finance and cared for the people. The truth is that the Chinese salt law focuses on taxation and adopts a heavy taxation system, taxing hundreds or even two thousand per hundred. If a no-tax system is adopted, any change is acceptable. Otherwise, the national economy is at stake, and production, sales, and transportation are all subject to established laws. Salt farmers and salt merchants each have their history and resources. Once destroyed, the overall network is lost, and both the country and the people suffer. This must be carefully considered. Implementing this new law will inevitably lead to difficulties. I will briefly outline the main points:

(A) Regarding the point of taxation at the field: According to the current salt law, salt is taxed first, regardless of whether it is in the field, the embankment, or the mound, and then a permit and transportation ticket are issued. The field has a responsible merchant, the shore has a responsible store, and the transportation has a registered boat. The starting point is filled in on the ticket, and no deviation is allowed. Inspections are conducted, and the system is well-organized with clear lines of authority and few agencies. The tax law is comprehensive. If taxation is at the field, as stipulated in Article 14 of Chapter 3 of the new law, the government should build warehouses and mounds in suitable locations in the salt fields for storing salt. The intention is that all salt produced by salt producers must be stored in government-designated warehouses and mounds in accordance with the provisions. Here are some questions: (1) Except for Sichuan and Yunnan, most salt-producing areas are coastal, and the salt fields are vast, covering thousands of square miles. How many warehouses and mounds should there be? Can they be fully equipped in the shortest possible time? Furthermore, with convenient water and land transportation, what good methods are there to completely block the path of smuggling? (2) For salt that is taxed after being stored in warehouses and mounds, will the water and land field police established in Article 34 of Chapter 6 be as effective as the field merchants in managing their stoves and investigating private sales with relevance and integrity? (3) Beach households, stove households, and board households are all poor people who want to get a price for their salt as soon as they have it. If the provisions of Article 23 of Chapter 4 of the new law are followed, the total amount of salt stored by salt producers should be allocated according to their annual production ratio. This means that salt producers must wait until a year later to get a price for their salt. Otherwise, it will be impossible to obtain their annual production ratio. How can poor people who have no surplus grain wait? Furthermore, taking five tons as the standard, all those who produce less than five tons have the priority to sell first. This means that those who are lazy and produce less have the priority, while those who are diligent and produce more are in a disadvantaged position. This is not a way to increase production and even encourages laziness. Not only that, but each field has hundreds or thousands of beach households, stove households, and board households. Should the salt of each household be divided into piles or gathered into a pile? If divided into piles, will there be enough space? If gathered into a pile, how will they be distinguished by household when sold in the future? How will they be distinguished as first-class or second-class salt? Furthermore, once the beach households, stove households, and board households have weighed and handed over their salt to the warehouse, will the tax officials provide insurance in case of natural disasters or man-made calamities? Since the date of salt sales varies, how will the differences in brine consumption be handled? Considering the interests of the salt farmers, storing salt in warehouses and mounds is troublesome and does not provide immediate cash to alleviate poverty. It is better to sit and sell privately, which is simpler and more convenient. Which would they prefer?

(B) Regarding the point of free buying and selling by the people: Under the current salt law, the people are not free, and merchants have no freedom. According to the current salt law, field merchants have the responsibility to provide funds for collection and storage, stove production has a designated merchant, and food households have a store for storage and supply. The purchase price and selling price are all determined by the government. Therefore, even if production is high, salt producers do not feel that their production is unsalable. Even if production is insufficient, food households do not feel that their food is particularly expensive. Even in poor rural areas and places with extremely difficult transportation, food households do not lack salt to eat. If the new law is followed, there will be no merchants, and the word "people" will include a very broad range. Allowing free buying and selling will raise questions. Are beach households, stove households, and board households people? Can they freely buy and sell? After taxation at the field, if free buying and selling are allowed, will there be no restrictions on the area? After taxation, will there still be restrictions on the salt leaving the field? Will it still be free? Furthermore, since there is no designated merchant, there is no responsible person. What methods can be used to restrict it? If free buying and selling are still subject to area and time limits specified on the tax ticket, then it will not be free. If there are no limits, there will be countless problems. Since it is free buying and selling, those who profit will continue to operate without encouragement, and those who suffer losses will be allowed to close down. If there is a salt shortage in area A, will sellers be allowed to raise prices? If there is a salt surplus in area B, will sellers be allowed to lower prices? In areas with convenient transportation, there will be many speculators, and will there be problems of congestion and losses? In areas with difficult transportation, will transporters be reluctant, and will food households suffer from a lack of salt? If grain is in short supply, one can still catch sparrows, dig for rats, and use grass roots and tree bark to fill the stomach. But what can replace salt if there is a salt shortage? Liu Yan's method was to store official salt in distant areas between the Yangtze and Lingnan. If merchants were cut off and salt was expensive, the price was reduced to stabilize the price. Can the government now establish stabilized-price warehouses everywhere?

(C) Regarding the point of reducing the tax to five yuan per 100 kilograms uniformly: Converted to the sima scale, 100 jin is equivalent to 3 yuan, 1 jiao, 7 fen, and 5 li plus some change. Salt is a daily necessity for the people and should be tax-free, just like rice and beans. In the past, it was said that the state cannot do without government expenses and therefore cannot avoid taxation. Also, the people's burden should be shared universally. But salt is less than food, and the production area is smaller than the grain-producing area. It is easy to manage because of its smallness, and it does not overburden the people. Therefore, abandoning grain tax in favor of salt tax is also a last resort. Today, the salt tax and surtax are heavy and extreme. Who would not want a reduction? But considering the state's budgetary situation, the good policy of a one-cent reduction in the likin tax has just been implemented. The financial difficulties of the central and local governments and the disputes over compensation have caused widespread unrest. After a sudden reduction in the salt tax, as well as the various tax exemptions for industrial and agricultural use of salt stipulated in Articles 6 and 7 of Chapter 1 of the new law, the leakage and abuses will be numerous. The central government will lose tens of millions of yuan in revenue each year, which is to be expected. In addition, various surcharges also generate an income of over 10,000 yuan each year. If these are all exempted, the total amount will probably be no less than 10 to several 10,000 yuan. How will this be supported? What methods will be used to compensate? Who will be responsible? This is something that those in power cannot ignore.

(D) Regarding the point of not allowing the sale of salt that does not meet standards and the implementation of discoloration and denaturation: Improving salt production is a natural principle of evolution and hygiene. It is acceptable to apply a gradual method to promote improvement. However, if the provisions of Article 4 of Chapter 1 of the new law are followed, salt containing 90% or more sodium chloride is considered first-class salt, and salt containing 85% or more sodium chloride is considered second-class salt. First-class salt should not contain more than 5% moisture, and second-class salt should not contain more than 8% moisture. This provision is somewhat presumptuous. Even in Japan, where science is advanced, the salt law stipulates that the sodium chloride content is divided into five grades, with the lowest being 70% or more and the highest being 90% or more. But in China, where science is backward, the grade and content are attempting to surpass Japan. The theory may be lofty, but how can the facts be difficult to implement? Furthermore, from a hygiene perspective, unclean impurities may be detrimental to hygiene, but what does moisture have to do with hygiene? Otherwise, water content will also be regulated when making ink. Also, salt containing magnesium is most likely to absorb moisture, and the seasons and weather are different. This is a natural chemical effect and not the fault of salt farmers and merchants. If this is implemented, then most of the salt already produced and not yet produced in each province will be unqualified and will have to be used entirely for fisheries, industry, and agriculture. However, fisheries, industry, and agriculture do not need such a large amount. Salt farmers rely on this for a living, so how will the government deal with this? Also, if the provisions of Article 18 of Chapter 3 of the new law are followed, salt that does not meet food salt standards should be stored separately for use in fisheries, industry, and agriculture, or the original producers should be ordered to re-produce it. I am afraid that salt farmers will admit that their salt does not meet the standards, not send it to the warehouses and mounds, and sell it all privately before being prohibited from selling it. If the law is not enforced on the masses, how will the government deal with it? Salt eaters are not all experts in hygiene; they only care about the salty taste and the cheap price. If the provisions of Article 29 of Chapter 5 of the new law are followed, and salt by-products such as bitter brine, brine blocks, brine nitrate crystals, alkali cakes, etc., are all tax-exempt, then any kind of by-product can be mixed with water and re-produced into salt. Anyone can take advantage of this, purchase these by-products to replace food salt, and what will become of the national salt tax? European and American countries either adopt a no-tax system or a light-tax system, so after discoloration and denaturation, they use heavy leaching and re-production procedures. The cost is not worthwhile, and there are very few abuses. The Chinese salt tax is particularly heavy, so even after discoloration and denaturation, it can be re-leached and re-produced after being transported out due to the tax exemption (the cost is still heavy at over three yuan per dan). Furthermore, Article 27 of Chapter 5 of the new law has a flexible method of not implementing discoloration and denaturation, which can be used for private gain. How can guarantees or deposits prevent abuses?

(E) Regarding the point of abolishing fields with low production, poor quality, and excessive costs in an appropriate manner: Eliminating salt fields through artificial means rather than natural means will not be effective. For example, the Liuzhuang field in Huaian has been abolished for many years because it is isolated from the sea, but private production continues as before. As for the coastal fields, although there were previously announcements of gradual abolition over five years and closure over three years, they have never been eliminated. Even in fields that have already been abolished, private production has risen, and the output is even greater than before abolition. This is clear. Smoke continues, and cooking stoves continue to burn. Everyone and every place has the means, and everyone and every place can produce salt and sell it privately. So, how can they be eliminated? In reality, it only facilitates private production and private sales.

(F) Regarding the point of the government limiting production based on the salt production situation to avoid overproduction: The salt production situation, like agriculture, depends on the weather. Whether salt production is excessive should also depend on sales. If restrictions are added, will abundance be suppressed to make it scarce, and will scarcity be forced to make it abundant? Will beach households, stove households, and board households be ordered to shut down and change careers after abundance, and can they be recruited at will after scarcity? Salt production is the livelihood of beach households, stove households, and board households, and they are familiar with the profits of salt production and private sales, which are a matter of life and death. Can they be tamed to this extent? Furthermore, the coastal salt fields east of the production area are boundless. If there is an abundant harvest, will it be abandoned on the ground or thrown into the sea? Otherwise, with higher costs and rail and water transportation available, only concentration will be seen, and no surplus will be seen. But the salt from Huai and Zhejiang, with high costs and long-distance transportation, will only be seen as excessive. Is there a plan to give all the benefits of the world to eastern Lu? Can the hundreds of thousands of beach households, stove households, and board households in Huai and Zhejiang and those who depend on them for a living be allowed to lose their jobs, cut off their livelihoods, and affect local security?

(G) Regarding the fact that the restrictions on production do not apply to refined salt companies, and even those who are re-refined are not subject to warehouse and mound restrictions, although it is said that taxes have already been paid for collection and release of salt, it cannot be unrelated. The unequal treatment clearly shows favoritism. The emergence of refined salt was to resist the import of foreign salt and was only allowed to be sold in commercial ports. If it infiltrated the interior, it would be considered private sales. The old law was very fair, but the companies thought it was inconvenient and clamored everywhere, promoting the abolition of the lead and free buying and selling every day. Now the Legislative Yuan holds this view. There are now more than ten companies, with a salt production volume of tens of thousands of dan. For example, Yongyu alone has a production quota of 1.5 million dan. If the lead is abolished, each company will expand greatly and emerge in succession. Only a dozen or so companies can monopolize the country's salt sales of 25 million dan. Northern salt is cheap and can be used to make salt, while southern salt is expensive and will inevitably use brine to make salt. The livelihoods of millions of salt farmers in the south will inevitably be seized by refined salt. Why is our government so generous to the dozen or so refined salt companies and so stingy to millions of salt farmers? This is truly baffling.

The above are just a few points to offer for study. If all questions have sufficient responses and solutions, then a reformist approach can be adopted and implemented resolutely. If there are no sufficient responses and solutions, then it is better to proceed cautiously, as a single mistake will be difficult to recover, harm the country and the people, and cause great damage, unlike other orders that can be easily reversed and remedied.

Letter 176

To the editor: I recently read a report in your newspaper's local news column stating that members of our regiment's first squad beat a ticket seller. This is inconsistent with the facts. I have recorded the actual situation at the time as reported by Wu Rugui, the captain of the first squad, and submit it as follows for your information: Yesterday afternoon, members of my squad wore uniforms and attended practice on time. After the practice, they dispersed and returned home. Some members had business in Shanghai and happened to take the Shanghai-Nanhui bus together. In accordance with the regiment's instructions, they purchased half-price tickets one by one. There were about thirty people at the time, and the Public Utility Bureau's regulation limited the capacity to twenty-eight people, so of course the limit could not be exceeded. The squad members and passengers already numbered over thirty, so there was a declaration restricting passengers to prevent danger, and there was no forced occupation. This is a clear fact. When the bus reached Maogong Bridge Station, a small number of squad members got off. The remaining members needed to go to Ximen, but the bus turned back to Longhua from the middle of the road near Jinji Road. According to the regulations of the No. 2 bus, the route runs from Ximen to Longhua and then from Longhua to Ximen. Of course, it cannot turn back halfway. This violated the company's regulations and deliberately made things difficult for the squad members. The members who wanted to go to Ximen did not reach their destination, so they inquired and asked the bus to go to Ximen in accordance with the regulations, which led to an argument. Upon hearing this, I immediately informed the members to return to the headquarters and wait for a resolution. The bus continued to run as usual without stopping, and there was no disturbance of order. The reports in the newspapers are inconsistent with the facts. I am reporting the facts and request that your newspaper correct the inaccurate reports to clarify the truth and avoid misunderstandings. Sincerely, Yang Xinzheng, Regiment Commander, Jing District Security Regiment

World News in Brief 177

— Hai Ke

▲In Central America, there is a race of red people. The men must absolutely obey the women. After marriage, the husband must leave his own family. He must pack all his belongings and move into his wife's home.

▲Since the strict implementation of prohibition in the United States, an alternative beverage has been created. This has greatly increased sugar consumption. The annual statistics show an alarming number.

▲Of the accidents that occur in London streets, 25 percent are caused by private cars hitting pedestrians. Trolleys and buses only account for 6 percent.

▲Parisian women, in order to enhance their beauty, often have their noses broken and ask beauty experts to reshape them. They can be customized to any desired style.

▲London once held a special exhibition. It featured two sisters who made a living from flower arranging. They used many English flowers in porcelain bowls to create small gardens. Visitors praised them greatly.

▲In Russia, there are more women than men. For every 1,000 men, there are 1,229 women. Germany is second, with 1,100 women per 1,000 men. Austria is next, with 1,069 women per 1,000 men.

Mourning Mr. Fan Shan 178

— Watch Cloud Tower Master

The passing of Mr. Fan Shan is deeply mourned by those who knew him and those who did not. I never met Mr. Fan Shan in person, but we corresponded frequently with poems. Mr. Fan Shan said my poems were clear and elegant, without the unintelligible language of modern poets, and he often praised them in front of his poet friends, which made me feel ashamed and grateful. I once wanted to call upon Mr. Fan Shan, introduced by Mr. Chen Yong'an, the Secretary of the Board from Guizhou, but Mr. Fan Shan politely declined, saying he would have his female disciple, Li Guifen, ask me about calligraphy. However, whenever I had questions, Mr. Fan Shan would explain them in detail, without acting as a teacher.

Mr. Fan Shan enjoyed listening to opera and his enthusiasm did not wane with age. Female opera singers from Tianjin visited him. Mr. Fan Shan knew that I also enjoyed listening to opera, so he introduced Li Guifen, Huiqin, Xue Yanqin, and others to me in letters when they came south, asking me to promote them. However, when Xin Yanqiu and Li Huiqin came to Shanghai last winter, I was bedridden and unable to write, so I only sent a message to wish them well. When Yanqiu returned north, she invited me to go with her, but I was too busy with matters in Shanghai. I planned to fulfill my wish this spring. If I had known this would happen, I would have gone north with Yanqiu at the end of the year and had a chance to meet Mr. Fan Shan. Now it is too late. How sad!

Last year, a Shanghai tabloid mistakenly reported the news of Mr. Fan Shan's death. At that time, Xue Yanqin had not been in Shanghai for long, and Mr. Fan Shan still wrote a letter to introduce her. So when I read the report, I was half in disbelief. Later, I wrote to the poet Cao Jiheng in Beijing and learned that it was not true. Mr. Fan Shan said that he had encountered this kind of strange rumor twice in his life. Last year was the third time. Mr. Yang Yunshi wrote an elegy for Mr. Fan Shan, for which Mr. Fan Shan was very grateful. When I received Mr. Heng's letter, I was happy that Mr. Fan Shan was not ashamed and had no health problems, so I also wrote a poem: "The news of the fall of the Old Man Star is on the newspaper, the message is half believed. Just see the high singing, full of enthusiasm, as if the living elegy does not seek poetry. Haiyun is happy to get a letter of peace, and the world will always keep the wonderful words. Countless thousands of miles from Jibei Jiangnan, a small heart remotely sent to the bright moon."

Guifen told me that Mr. Fan Shan looked clear and refined, like a man in his sixties. He liked to sniff snuff, and his mustache was always stained with the color of snuff. His fingers were not very clean either. It is generally the case that scholars do not pay attention to their appearance. Mr. Fan Shan's bedroom was full of books, in a chaotic state. However, Mr. Fan Shan had a strong memory and could easily find the books he needed. Therefore, he did not allow his family to organize this pile of books, because after organizing them, it would be inconvenient to find them.

After Mr. Fan Shan's death, young people made presumptuous comments on his poetry. Regardless of praise or criticism, they are not worth taking seriously. In short, Mr. Fan Shan's poetry and lyrics formed his own style, comparable to his predecessors. His poem discussing poetry with Zuo Huqing shows his approach to poetry, which cannot be dreamed of by shallow scholars. The poem says: "Don't you see Lanzi's seven swords in both hands, five of which are always in the air. Skilled hands can use emptiness to operate reality, opening the chaos into exquisite beauty. Don't you see Shanfu planting flowers in Lihua Palace, the colors of ten thousand flowers are not the same. Ingenious hands can use plainness to create splendor, making the desolate return to spring. Military strategists use few to overcome many, politicians use light to lift heavy. Taoists use stillness to control movement, poets use uniqueness to overcome the common. Able to say what others cannot say, like a mountain revealing its spirit without concealment. Able to complete what others cannot complete, like the moon hanging in the sky on the fifteenth day. A hundred buckets will not exhaust the spring at the bottom of the well, and burning will not extinguish the incense. A hundred flowers are brewed into a bottle of wine, and a hundred medicines are refined into a pill. Take the sweetness of the five flavors, the freshness of the five colors, and the harmony of the five sounds. Only the appearance is not uniquely beautiful. Take it from Du Su, the foundation is solid. Take it from Bai Lu, the courtyard is wide. Take it from Wen Li, the thoughts are abundant. Take it from Huang Chen, the profound is penetrated. Words have substance, filling the cake. Cut it into a picture, weaving on the loom. See it without a trace, like salt in water. Release it and it flies, like a sword in a box. Without intention, how can you create a classic? Without a pen, how can you command ten thousand spirits? Without talent, how can you gather heroes? Without learning, how can you achieve old age? Without law, what is a ruler? Without cause, what is weight? If one word is not safe, everyone will criticize it. Who cannot be attacked from all sides? Old Hu Zaoyan challenged yesterday, intending to follow Han Tong's changes. More than sixty years of poor life, I will use the dragon-carving debate for you. The forest of poetry is a hundred feet pole, and the progress of the elderly is like that of the young. Those who learn from me will die, it is not so. If my words are true, poetry will be immortal."

New Construction in Suzhou Park 179

— Planning

Suzhou Park was rebuilt on the old site of the abandoned Prince's mansion in the city. It has been four years since its establishment. There are two teahouses on either side of the fountain in the south, called East Study and West Pavilion. North of the West Pavilion is the movie theater. Tourists gather here. The northern area is twice the size of the southern area, but no one goes there because of the weeds. When the former Rain King Yincai was the chief host of the Suzhou Municipal Preparatory Office, he planned to find a way to develop it, but he failed due to lack of funds. Now, Chief Huang Shen, the county magistrate, has allocated funds to dig a pond in the open space north of the library for lotuses. The excavated mud is piled on the banks of the pond, with more than a hundred peach and willow trees planted on top, and rocks are piled up to form a small mountain. There is an open space left on top to build a house. This work has now been completed. Therefore, the number of tourists in the north has recently been no less than that in the south.

Strange Records of Childbirth 180

— Li Xufan

Difficult births of monstrous fetuses are often heard of. Families who give birth to them often consider them unlucky. If they die, they are buried and forgotten. If they live, they are abandoned to die. This rarely provides an opportunity for physiological research. The second daughter of a neighboring Yin family married Kang Sanguan of Cangqiao, Songjiang. For ten years, Kang has been hoping to have a child, but has been disappointed. Now, fortunately, she is six months pregnant. On March 9, she suddenly felt unusually abdominal pain. Counting the pregnancy period, it has been more than two months. She quickly hired a midwife to prepare everything. After a day and night, she finally gave birth. The baby was born buttocks first, which is called "sitting horse birth". This type of difficult birth is very dangerous. After more than an hour, the baby fell to the ground with a cry. Looking at it, it was a unicorn. They were very happy. The child's head was as big as a child's, and its hands were very long, reaching past its knees. There was a dimple on its back, like Meng's. At first, they were even happier because of its strange appearance. After bathing its whole body, they lifted its lip and saw two incisors. Touching it, it chirped like a bird, unable to cry. Sanguan was surprised. His wife was very angry, suspecting it was a monster. She threw it to the ground, and its face slowly turned blue. Kang's elderly mother was eager to have a grandchild and could not bear to abandon it. She quickly carried it to the bed, and its face turned from blue to reddish-brown. Just as she was about to see what was going on, within two hours, teeth grew all over its mouth. Kang's wife was even more panicked, fearing that a great disaster was about to befall them, and the whole family was in an uproar. The ignorant elders in the neighborhood added fuel to the fire, saying it was a monster. Kang's mother also lost her mind. As a result, they abandoned it in the Cangqiao River. It is said that the mother is now critically ill.

New Inventions for Waste Utilization 181

— Frugal Father

The study of calligraphy relies entirely on copying. Recently, paper has become expensive, making it uneconomical to buy paper for calligraphy practice. Furthermore, thin paper is easily torn when inked, making it difficult to reuse. If discarded casually, it would violate the principle of cherishing resources. Now there is a way to solve this problem, which is to use newspapers for copying. When I was teaching in Ping'a, I subscribed to several Shanghai newspapers for browsing. Whenever I practiced calligraphy, I used newspapers as trial paper. Because newspaper paper is thicker, ink does not easily bleed through the back, allowing for repeated copying. After writing, expose it to the sun to dry. After the ink is dry, fold and sell it. Compared to the market price, it is not much less. I have also tried this with my students, and it has been effective. Those who share the same hobby, why not try it?

Recently, German-style "Phoebus" gas stoves have become essential items for home and travel. However, the rubber on the gas needle often shrinks and hardens due to prolonged heat exposure, causing the gas to lose its effectiveness. Users are bothered by this. Although the retailer can replace it, it costs four or five cents and does not last long. Recently, I found a method that has proven effective. The method is to use an old, broken shoe sole (rubber or plastic soles are not suitable). Use a sharp blade to cut it thin and cut out a circular piece. Cut a slit in the middle. Force it onto the tip of the needle. Then tighten the screw and fold the leather forward. Use your hands to tightly insert it into the cylinder and pull it back and forth a few times, and it will be in place. This method does not require any cost and is durable. Once tested, you will know that my words are not wrong.

Wu Ziyu's Voice of Going Abroad 182

— Shi Yan Ye

General Wu Ziyu of Penglai, believing in military force, has retreated to Jigong Mountain since his defeat at Yuguan in the thirteenth year. Then to Luoyang, then to Nanyang. In the end, as the National Army unified the north and south, he fled into the Wushan Mountains for seven or eight years. He once disguised himself as a monk and twice attempted suicide. The end of a hero is truly sad and difficult. The people of the country despise him for his undying ambition, but many admire him for not seeking refuge with foreigners. Now, it is reported that the General will go abroad. He sent an envoy to Beijing, requesting to go under the guise of investigation, and wanting 100,000 gold to strengthen his journey. The National Government is also broad-minded, and there is talk of granting his request. Then the General will soon travel across the ocean to take a look at the new world overseas and breathe the new air of the world. However, according to what visitors from Sichuan have said, Wu does not seem to want to be an overseas passerby, but wants to be a resident on the edge of the sea. Friends from Sichuan said that Wu lives in the Wen Tianxiang Shrine in Xuanhan, relying on Liu Cunhou's monthly allowance of 2,000 gold for living expenses. In recent years, there have been many disturbances in Sichuan, and officials and civilians alike are in difficult circumstances. Liu's assistance is always in danger of being stopped at any time. Although Liu could not bear to issue an eviction order, Wu ultimately felt that it was not a long-term plan to live under someone else's roof. Many of his followers had given up hope for the future and were scattered. He felt that he could not stay here for a day. Last year, he wrote to Sun, a trusted acquaintance in Shanghai, saying that Sichuan was difficult, and it was useless to stay. It was better to return to his hometown than to die in a foreign land. Please tell Penglai to repair his thatched cottage immediately, just needing a few thatched houses to provide a place to live and read in his old age, which would be enough. At the end of the letter, he also included a poem, which said: "I search for my old residence in the fragrance of winter wine, how are the dreams of the past? After twenty years of iron horses, I return to the remaining years of my life, reading books in the remaining water and mountains." His letter and poem were all aimed at returning home, but today's newspaper reports say otherwise. I think that going abroad and returning home are both paths of self-awareness, but returning home after going abroad is even more advisable. Does the General agree?

▲Publishing News: "Movie Life," edited by Tang Bihua, exclusively publishes interesting anecdotes and news about Chinese and foreign movie stars, and publishes the long novel "Unofficial History of Movies" by Su Liu Mountain House in installments. It is richly illustrated, beautifully printed, has concise writing, and is extremely interesting. The tenth issue was published yesterday, priced at 15 cents per copy. The special subscription price for the whole year is 4 yuan and 40 cents, and six glossy celebrity photos are given as a gift. It is distributed by the Bolan Bookstore in Penglai Market, Nanshi.

▲Publishing News: Recently, many comrades in the literary and art circles have launched the "Da Guang Bao." The inaugural issue is scheduled to be released (the fourth). The purpose is pure, the material is elegant, and it focuses on art, with real society as the background. It avoids low-level interests and implies deep meaning in the ordinary. It reveals true heart through games. The office is located at 114 Yunnan Road.

Travels in India (16) 183

— Ling Hua

Tigers, leopards, rhinoceroses, and elephants are all produced in India, but Ceylon produces especially many elephants. Snakes of all kinds are found everywhere in India. Their customs include worshiping elephants, lions, and snakes. White horses are often seen. I remember that in the time of Emperor Ming of the Han Dynasty, Buddhist scriptures first came to China, carried by white horses to the Eastern Capital. Therefore, Luoyang has the White Horse Temple. I don't know if this temple still exists today. It shows that India has had white horses since ancient times. I came to India and saw a large white bullock cart and a white horse. It made me think of the book "Journey to the West." Although it is absurd, it seems to have some basis. It narrates Tang Sanzang's journey to the Western Paradise to obtain scriptures, with Pigsy, White Dragon Horse, Sand Monk, and Monkey King. Now, facts prove it. White horses carried scriptures. India still has white horses today. This is a fact. Pigsy passed through Muslim countries on his way to India. Muslims abstain from pork, hence the name. Sand Monk is a novice monk. Monkey King is the name of a monkey. Today, there are many people playing with monkeys on the streets of India. It can be seen that the author of "Journey to the West" did not completely fabricate it and should not be taken lightly. Also, the "evil demon king" is also reasonable. The Three Thousand Buddhas Sutra has the title of Bull King Buddha, which was said by the Buddha. Indians worship cattle and often decorate them with brocade. The large horns of the cattle are also very beautiful. Also, the cattle resemble camels, with high, protruding humps under their necks, which is different from China. Calling them "demon kings" is not without reason. As for the "Land of Women," it is even more of a fact. Java and other places were still female kingdoms in the Yuan Dynasty. Qinghai, Tibet, and Burma still have women today. It is just that the novel naturally embellishes its words. Also, the mention of passing through flames refers to the many volcanoes in various places today. From this, it can be proved that ancient books should not be regarded as absurd in general. They should have a considerable basis and then be embellished to create interesting texts.

Indian chickens, cats, and dogs are generally no different. However, I remember often hearing my mother say that Tang Sanzang brought cats to China to open the way for the Daoist priest. The Daoist priest said that China must have had cats before the Tang Dynasty. But Tang Dynasty poetry does not seem to have the word "cat." The ancient "Book of Songs" says, "There are cats and tigers." Interpreters refer to tigers as large beasts, not small cats. Then, perhaps the saying that cats came from the West is not entirely unfounded.

I happened to see a donkey on a Chinese street. I don't know if it was brought by the Chinese or if India has them. I will have to inquire.

Indians abstain from killing many mice. There are eagles all over the sky in Calcutta, but they are not seen caring about them. I often believe in Confucius's teaching that "Are humans inferior to birds?" After investigating in all aspects, the morality of birds is always higher than that of beasts. And humans are mammals, so their inferiority to birds is also due to something. I saw someone selling parrots and asked the price. One small parrot costs 15 yuan, and another costs 200 yuan. This is probably because the cost of living is high here.

Recently, I asked an Indian friend, and he said that there are many donkeys in India, which is not surprising. I obtained this evidence and proved it. First, it proves that donkeys can still be freely raised in tropical India. Second, I remember reading Spencer's diary, in which he said that he rode a donkey in Egypt. In ancient times, Jesus often rode a donkey in Judah. Then the donkey species from India to Egypt can all survive. Why do the people of Guangdong, Guangxi, and Guizhou tell me that donkey hooves are thin and cannot withstand heat and cannot be raised? It is probably because the sages spread the donkey species. It is not easy to prove a small thing. Dr. Sun Yat-sen's theory of "knowing is difficult and doing is easy" is valuable. I hope that the people of the south will quickly raise more donkeys to increase production, so that the burden on the people's shoulders can be lightened.

Finance: Interest Rates Steady, Foreign Silver Soars 184

Yesterday was still within the sealing period. Banks had not yet opened. In the money market, the interest rate for foreign silver was 7 qian, 2 fen, 5 li and a half in the morning market, and 7 qian, 2 fen, 5 li and 7 hao in the afternoon market. The results were the same as the previous afternoon. The silver interest rate was 2 fen in both the morning and afternoon markets. The amount of foreign exchange bills was 735,000 in the morning market, with no transactions for banknotes. In the afternoon market, the amount of foreign exchange bills was 570,000, and 5,000 for banknotes. Outside the market, the amount of banknotes was 144,000 in the morning market and 65,000 in the afternoon market. The money shops collected and delivered more than 7.4 million in silver public orders and more than 4.1 million in silver public orders. Small money shops traded more than 500,000 in banknotes and remittances, and collected and delivered more than 800,000 in remittances from various routes. In the morning market, the small foreign silver from Jiangnan remained the same at 6 qian, 3 fen and 9 li, with limited transactions, only 2,000 jiao. In the afternoon market, it was stirred up by the Guangdong silver and rose sharply, breaking through the 4 fen mark to 6 qian, 4 fen and 1 li, with transactions of 9,500 jiao. The price of Guangdong small foreign silver rose sharply due to purchases. The price in the morning market even reached 6 qian, 4 fen and 1 li, an increase of 3 li and a half compared to the afternoon market the previous day. The afternoon market fell slightly by 1 li, calculated at 6 qian, 4 fen and 2 li, with transactions of 220,000 jiao in the morning market and 170,000 jiao in the afternoon market. Copper coins remained at 369,000 cash.

It is expected that the standard yarn market tomorrow will not change greatly if the overseas situation is difficult to change, or there may be a tendency to rise. ▲ The China Products Tobacco Company announces: Our company held its first annual shareholders' meeting yesterday at our factory located at 91 Avenue Road. Youth Corner

The Jinda Cycling Tour Group Undertakes a 1,500-Li Journey 192

— Guo Rui

It was about a week ago that Jinan University students were excitedly discussing the upcoming spring break, pondering how to spend their leisure time. Some thought, "A short trip nearby would be convenient," while others thought, "A long trip involving mountain climbing and wading through rivers would broaden my horizons." Therefore, the destinations decided upon by the students varied. Naturally, some were going to Hangzhou, Suzhou, Nanjing, or Nanxiang.

However, some students believed that traveling by boat or train was monotonous and uninteresting, lacking the true meaning of travel. They also felt that young people should possess a brave and vibrant spirit and strive for "constant progress and self-improvement." So they organized a free tour group, with a route from Shanghai to Suzhou, Wuxi, Zhenjiang, and then Nanjing. From Nanjing, they would then go to Hangzhou, Ningbo, Zhenhai, Putuo Mountain, and return to Shanghai. The journey would be a full 1,500 li and would require about two weeks.

But their tour group could also be called a "ten-person group," because the tour group was made up of only ten experienced cyclists, with no accompanying staff. So their clothing, food, lodging, and transportation were entirely self-managed. Furthermore, the amount subsidized by the school was not large, so their 1,500-li journey, though not as grand and magnificent as the previous journeys of children walking to Nanyang and the Northeast, their spirit of bravery and vigor was worthy of being mentioned in the same breath.

Letter to the Youth Corner 193

Editor,

This manuscript is my first offering. Please publish it and don't set it aside, lest I be greatly disappointed. That would be very pitiful. Please forgive me for my poor writing, because my level is very low. I won't say much more. Wishing you literary peace. [Signed] Bei Chan

Suffering

Poor her, her brows are furrowed all day long, as if she has many worries. She always sleeps in that dark little room. Sometimes she doesn't know what she is thinking, and she grasps a pen and starts to write. But when she gets halfway, she stops writing. She reads it from the beginning and then tears it up with a "whoosh" and throws it into the wastepaper basket. Sometimes others piece together her torn paper to look at it. It is always a lament of fate, a sigh of bitterness.

Her mother is a tyrant in the family, lying in bed all day, scolding almost from morning until she sleeps. Hearing this hateful sound in her ears is like being cut by knives. Endless sorrows, strand by strand, float in her heart. Tears stream down her face. Her lover is economically weak. Although he pities her and understands her in every way, he cannot satisfy her vain mother. Unable to please her elders, she naturally cannot achieve her free love and marriage. Poor her, she cannot disobey her mother, and she has much attachment to her lover. Such a situation easily leads her to be pessimistic. She wants to be self-reliant, but she has no introducer and no skills to apply for jobs. She stays in the dark family, with no hope of getting out. Poor her, living this kind of life, she sheds countless tears every day. Sometimes her mother even says that she is useless, just sitting at home eating. In fact, this kind of woman is the most tormented. She has no ability to be independent, and no ability to talk about civilization and freedom. Her weak soul is like being tossed by a whirlwind. She has no heart to read, and no one to share her sorrows with. The so-called lover cannot have a frank conversation with her or go out to see movies. She has hardly any means of amusement to eliminate her worries. Her mother does not have a single word of sympathy for her, only unintentional scolding. There are also ignorant people nearby who laugh at them and fabricate bad things about her in front of her mother, making her even more sad.
